Refutation of the Claim that the Imam Must Know the Unseen
Al-Nasafi refutes the claim that the imam must know the unseen and states the proper qualifications for imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why requiring the imam to know the unseen elevates the caliphate above prophethood and constitutes disbelief.

Core Idea
Requiring the imam to know the unseen places the caliphate above prophethood, which is pure disbelief.

Al-Nasafi confronts a sectarian claim that the imam must possess knowledge of the unseen. He dismisses it as absurd and then provides a decisive argument based on the nature of imamate as succession to prophethood. This passage teaches us the proper scope of knowledge required for leadership.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
Pay attention to the tone of reductio ad absurdum.
2
Identify the two absurd claims
Notice how al-Nasafi compares the claim that the imam must know the unseen to the even more absurd claim that the imam's dog must be infallible.
This rhetorical device exposes the unreasonableness of the first claim.
3
Understand the positive argument
Al-Nasafi states that the imam's knowledge should be limited to what is necessary for executing the affairs of the subjects. All else is unnecessary.
4
Grasp the key proof from prophethood
The imamate is a caliphate of prophethood. Since the Prophet himself distinguished between religious and worldly knowledge, requiring the imam to exceed this limit would elevate the caliphate above prophethood.
The hadith 'You know best your worldly affairs' is central.
5
Reflect on the consequence
The passage concludes that demanding the imam know the unseen or worldly affairs is pure disbelief (kufr), as it reverses the hierarchy.
This shows the gravity of the error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأنه قال: بعضهم أن الإمام ينبغي أن يعلم الغيب، وهذا كما حكي عن بعضهم ينبغي أن يكون كلب الإمام معصوما وهذا تجاهل، ومن بلغ في الغباء هذه الغاية يعرض عن مناظرته. ثم علم الإمام يحتاج إليه لتنفيذ أمور الرعية، فما وراء ذلك من العلوم لا معنى لاشتراطه. يحققه أن الإمامة خلافة النبوة والنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: أنا أعلم بأمور دينكم وأنتم أعلم بأمور دنياكم فمن شرط أن يكون الإمام عالما بأمور الدنيا أو يعلم الغيب فقد جعل درجة الخلافة أعلى من درجة النبوة، وهذا كفر محض.
And he said: Some of them [say] that the imam ought to know the unseen. And this is like what is related from some of them: the imam's dog ought to be infallible. And this is ignorance, and whoever reaches this extreme in stupidity turns away from debating him. Then the imam's knowledge is needed for executing the affairs of the subjects; beyond that, there is no meaning to stipulating [other] sciences. He verifies it [by saying] that the imamate is a caliphate of prophethood, and the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'I know best concerning your religious affairs, and you know best concerning your worldly affairs.' So whoever stipulates that the imam be knowledgeable in worldly affairs or know the unseen has made the rank of the caliphate higher than the rank of prophethood, and this is pure disbelief.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that an imam must have knowledge of the unseen (ghayb). Al-Nasafi begins by likening this claim to an even more absurd one, that the imam's dog must be infallible, thereby highlighting the baselessness of the demand. He then argues that the imam's required knowledge is limited to what is necessary for administering the affairs of the people; there is no point in stipulating additional knowledge such as the unseen. To seal the refutation, he invokes the decisive argument: the imamate is a succession (khilāfa) of prophethood. The Prophet himself distinguished between religious and worldly knowledge, deferring to his companions in worldly matters. Requiring the imam to know the unseen or worldly affairs would place the caliphate above prophethood, which is outright disbelief (kufr). Thus the claim is not only false but repugnant to the very principle of succession.

Key Terms
الإمامة
الخلافة
الغيب
النبوة
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the imam must be omniscient or have knowledge of the unseen.
Correction: The imam's knowledge is limited to what is needed for governance; demanding more violates the principle that imamate is caliphate of prophethood.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, what is the consequence of stipulating that the imam know the unseen?
A) It makes the imamate impossible to fill.
B) It elevates the caliphate above prophethood, which is kufr.
C) It contradicts the consensus of the Companions.
D) It is permissible as long as the imam is just.

Key Takeaway
The imam's knowledge is limited to administrative needs; requiring more such as unseen knowledge undermines prophethood and is disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever expected a leader (imam, scholar, or even a family member) to have knowledge of your personal unseen affairs—expecting them to know what only Allah knows? How does Al-Nasafi's argument expose the danger of such an expectation in your own heart? What step will you take to rectify this attitude today?
?
In your life, do you tend to give more weight to worldly expertise than to religious guidance when choosing whom to follow? This passage warns that demanding worldly knowledge from the imam elevates the caliphate above prophethood. Where have you done this, and how can you realign your priorities to honor the prophetic model?
?
Are you willing to accept that your leaders are fallible in worldly matters, as the Prophet himself said 'You know best your worldly affairs'? What does your reaction to their mistakes reveal about your understanding of leadership as a caliphate? Commit to one practical way you will lower your expectations of leaders in worldly matters, focusing instead on their role in executing the affairs of the community.

The Imam Need Not Be the Most Excellent: Maturidi Position on Afdaliyya
Al-Nasafi states the Maturidi position, reports Ash'ari view, and provides proof from the caliphal selection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position on whether the imam must be the most excellent person of his time, and the evidence from the shura of 'Umar.

Core Idea
Imamate requires suitability, not supreme excellence; practical benefit outweighs theoretical preference.

In this passage from al-Tabsira, al-Nasafi presents a key point of Maturidi political theology: the imam need not be the most excellent (afdal) of his time. He contrasts this with the Ash'ari view and grounds his argument in the practice of the Companions, especially 'Umar's appointment of the shura council. This lesson examines the reasoning and evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two views
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note that Al-Nasafi first states the Maturidi view and lists other groups who hold it, then presents the Ash'ari position and their reasoning.
Pay attention to the key terms: الأفضلية (afdaliyya) and المفضول (mafdūl).
2
Understand the Maturidi proof from 'Umar's shura
Al-Nasafi provides a historical proof: when 'Umar was stabbed, he appointed a shura of six men despite the manifest superiority of some (like 'Uthman and 'Ali). This shows that the most excellent need not be chosen.
The proof emphasizes practical benefit (maslaha) and capability over abstract excellence.
3
Reflect on the practical argument about knowledge
The passage concludes that true superiority is known only to Allah, so attaching the imamate to something unknowable is impractical. Reflect on how this supports the Maturidi position.
This argument counters the Ash'ari analogy with prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما كونه أفضل أهل زمانه ليس بشرط عندنا نص عليه الشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله في كتاب المقالات، بل إذا كان فاضلا صالحا للإمامة وعقدت له الإمامة انعقدت، وإن كان الأفضل منه موجودا، وإليه ذهبت المعتزلة والحسين بن الفضل البجلي من متكلمي أهل الحديث وأبو العباس القلانسي ومحمد بن إسحق بن خزيمة. وذهب أبو الحسن الأشعري بأن إمامة المفضول لا تنعقد مع وجود الفاضل، ويقول: إن من الأوصاف التي يصير بها المرء أهلا للإمامة أن لا يكون أحد من أهل زمانه أفضل منه، فإذا وجد الأفضل لم يثبت للمفضول أهلية الإمامة، ويقولون أيضا إن الأفضل أقرب إلى انقياد النفوس إلى متابعته، وإيثار طاعته والائتمار لأوامره أمكن وأميل ويقولون: إن الإمامة يطلب فيها الفضل فيجب أن يطلب لها على رتبة فيه قياسا على النبوة. إلا أن أصحابنا رحمهم الله احتجوا أن عمر لما طعن الله جعل الخلافة شورى بين ستة نفر مع ظهور فضيلة بعضهم على بعض، ولم يعين الأفضل منهم بل فوض إليهم ليختاروا من كانت المصلحة بإمامته أعم للخلق، ومن كان أقدر على القيام بما فوض القيام به إلى الإمام وإن كان غيره أفضل منه في نفسه، وهذا لأن كون عثمان وعلي رضي الله عنهما أفضل ممن دخل معهما في الشورى كان ظاهرا إنما الالتباس كان في أن قيام أيهم بأمور الأمة ومصالح المسلمين أنفع لهم وأعود وأعم فائدة وأتم عائدة، ففوض إليهم ذلك لينظروا فيه فيقلدوا الإمامة أصلحهم لذلك وكذا بعد الخلفاء الراشدين إلى يومنا هذا عقدت الخلافة لإنسان، وفي قريش من هو أفضل منه وأورع وأتقى وأعلم، ورأى الناس إمامهم في كل زمان مفترض الطاعة على أن لا وجه لمعرفة فضيلة أحد على طريق الحقيقة عند الله تعالى، بل هو أمر يثبت بالاجتهاد وغالب الظن فيه فتعليق الحكم به تعليق بما لا يمكن القيام به والحاجة إلى معرفة ذلك بالناس ماسة، إذ الخلافة تثبت بعقدهم واختيارهم، فإذا كان لا يمكنهم الوقوف على ذلك حقيقة لم يكن
As for his being the most excellent of his time, it is not a condition according to us—Shaykh Abu Mansur, may Allah have mercy on him, has explicitly stated that in the Book of Articles. Rather, if he is virtuous and suitable for the imamate and the imamate is contracted for him, it is contracted, even if one more excellent than him exists. And this is the view of the Mu'tazila, al-Husayn ibn al-Fadl al-Bajali from the theologians of ahl al-hadith, Abu al-Abbas al-Qalanisi, and Muhammad ibn Ishaq ibn Khuzayma. Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari held that the imamate of the inferior is not valid when the superior exists. He says: among the qualities by which a person becomes qualified for the imamate is that there should not be anyone from his time more excellent than him. So when the superior exists, the inferior does not have qualification for imamate. They also say that the superior is more likely to lead to the submission of souls to follow him, preferring his obedience, and complying with his commands—more possible and more inclined. And they say: excellence is sought in imamate, so it is necessary to seek it at a high level in him by analogy with prophethood. However, our companions, may Allah have mercy on them, argued that when 'Umar was stabbed, he made the caliphate a consultation (shura) among six men, despite the manifest superiority of some over others. He did not designate the most excellent but delegated to them to choose the one whose imamate would bring broader benefit to the people and who was more capable of carrying out what is entrusted to the imam, even if another was more excellent in himself. This is because the fact that 'Uthman and 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with them, were more excellent than those included with them in the shura was apparent; rather, the ambiguity lay in which of them would be more beneficial and advantageous for the people, greater in benefit and more complete in return. So he left it to them to examine and appoint the most suitable. Similarly, after the Rightly Guided Caliphs to our own day, the caliphate has been contracted for a man while among Quraysh there is someone more excellent, more pious, more God-fearing, and more knowledgeable. And people have seen their imam in every age as one whose obedience is obligatory, and there is no way to truly know the superiority of anyone with respect to Allah the Exalted. Rather, it is something established by ijtihad and probable opinion. So attaching the ruling to it is attaching it to something impossible to realize, and people have urgent need for knowledge of that, since the caliphate is established by their contract and choice. So if they cannot ascertain that truly, it is not...
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage presents the Maturidi position on the condition of afdaliyya (being the most excellent) for the imamate. It is a three-part argument: (1) the position of the Maturidis and others, (2) the opposing Ash'ari view, and (3) the proof from our school. Al-Nasafi begins by stating that being the most excellent is not a condition, citing Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, and lists other groups holding this view. He then presents the Ash'ari view that the imamate of an inferior (mafdūl) is invalid when a superior (fāḍil) exists, along with their reasoning: the superior is more likely to command obedience, and excellence is required by analogy with prophethood. Finally, he gives the proof of the Maturidis: 'Umar appointed a six-man shura without designating the most excellent, and later caliphs were chosen despite the presence of more excellent individuals. Moreover, true superiority is known only to Allah, and attaching the imamate to something unknowable is impractical. Thus the condition of afdaliyya is not necessary.

Key Terms
الأفضلية
المفضول
الشورى
الإمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the most excellent person must always be the imam.
Correction: The Maturidis argue that suitability and practical benefit are more important, as shown by 'Umar's shura which included less excellent individuals.

Checkpoint
What is the main evidence the Maturidis use to prove that the imam need not be the most excellent?
A) The Prophet's hadith about worldly and religious knowledge.
B) The appointment of a shura by 'Umar among six men including less excellent ones.
C) The consensus of the Ash'aris.
D) The superiority of the first four caliphs over all others.

Key Takeaway
The imamate is not contingent on being the most excellent; rather, practical governance and public interest determine suitability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you seek leadership or influence in your community, do you measure yourself by comparison to others (who is 'better') or by how well you can serve the real needs of the people? What would it take for you to genuinely prioritize practical benefit over personal excellence?
?
The passage argues that true superiority is known only to Allah. Think of a person you have judged as 'less worthy' of a role. How does this lesson challenge that judgment? Will you actively suspend your comparisons and trust communal decision-making instead?
?
The shura of 'Umar left the choice to a council despite clear differences in virtue. Are you willing to submit to collective choices even when you believe you know who the 'best' person is? Where in your life do you need to exercise this humility?

The Hanafi Proof Against Requiring the Most Excellent Imam
Hanafi proof against requiring the most excellent imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Hanafi/Maturidi argument that practical benefit and capability in leadership take precedence over personal excellence in the imam.

Core Idea
Leadership is about benefit, not personal virtue.

The Hanafi school presents a compelling proof that the imam does not have to be the most excellent person. Using the historical event of ‘Umar’s shūrā committee, they argue that practical capacity for governance and general benefit are the decisive criteria. Let’s examine their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the flow: first the historical precedent, then the reasoning, then a contrast with prophethood.
2
Identify the historical precedent
Focus on the story of ‘Umar’s shura committee. Why did he include both excellent and less excellent companions? What does this teach about selecting an imam?
The key point: he did not appoint the most excellent but left choice to the group.
3
Understand the reasoning about benefit vs virtue
The text says the ambiguity was about who would be most beneficial, not about who was most virtuous. This establishes that maṣlaḥa (benefit) and capability are the criteria.
Compare to the later statement that true excellence is known only to Allah.
4
Compare imamate to prophethood
The passage contrasts imamate (human choice) with prophethood (divine choice). In prophethood, Allah directly selects the most excellent; in imamate, we cannot know hidden virtue, so we rely on apparent benefit.
This distinction is central to the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا أن أصحابنا - رحمهم الله - احتجوا أن عمر لما طعن الله جعل الخلافة شورى بين ستة نفر مع ظهور فضيلة بعضهم على بعض، ولم يعين الأفضل منهم بل فوض إليهم ليختاروا من كانت المصلحة بإمامته أعم للخلق، ومن كان أقدر على القيام بما فوض القيام به إلى الإمام وإن كان غيره أفضل منه في نفسه، وهذا لأن كون عثمان وعلي - رضي الله عنهما - أفضل ممن دخل معهما في الشورى كان ظاهرا إنما الالتباس كان في أن قيام أيهم بأمور الأمة ومصالح المسلمين أنفع لهم وأعود وأعم فائدة وأتم عائدة، ففوض إليهم ذلك لينظروا فيه فيقلدوا الإمامة أصلحهم لذلك. وكذا بعد الخلفاء الراشدين إلى يومنا هذا عقدت الخلافة لإنسان، وفي قريش من هو أفضل منه وأورع وأتقى وأعلم، ورأى الناس إمامهم في كل زمان مفترض الطاعة على أن لا وجه لمعرفة فضيلة أحد على طريق الحقيقة عند الله تعالى، بل هو أمر يثبت بالاجتهاد وغالب الظن فيه فتعليق الحكم به تعليق بما لا يمكن القيام به والحاجة إلى معرفة ذلك بالناس ماسة، إذ الخلافة تثبت بعقدهم واختيارهم، فإذا كان لا يمكنهم الوقوف على ذلك حقيقة لم يكن لتعليق الحكم به فائدة بخلاف النبوة، فإن الله تعالى هو الذي يختار من يشاء من عباده لرسالته ونبوته، وهو العالم بحقيقة كل شيء، فكان من اختاره من أهل زمانه لرسالته وتحميل أمانته أفضل خليقته وأكمل بريته في وقته، وفيما نحن فيه الأمر بخلافه، والله تعالى الموفق
However, our companions - may Allah have mercy on them - argued that when ‘Umar was stabbed, Allah made the caliphate a consultation among six men despite the apparent superiority of some over others, and he did not appoint the most excellent among them; rather, he delegated to them to choose the one whose imamate would be of the most general benefit for the creatures, and the one most capable of undertaking what was entrusted to the imam, even if another was more excellent in himself. This is because it was apparent that ‘Uthmān and ‘Alī - may Allah be pleased with them - were more excellent than those who entered the consultation with them; the ambiguity was only regarding which of them would be more beneficial and more useful for the affairs of the community and the interests of the Muslims, and more complete in benefit. So he delegated that to them to consider and then appoint as imam the one most suitable for that. Similarly, after the Rightly Guided Caliphs until our day, the caliphate has been contracted to a person, while among Quraysh there are those who are more excellent, more pious, more God-fearing, and more knowledgeable. And the people consider their imam in every time to be obligatory to obey, while there is no way to know the superiority of anyone truly before Allah the Exalted; rather, it is a matter established by ijtihād and predominant opinion. So attaching the ruling to it is attaching to something that cannot be undertaken, while the need for people to know that is pressing, since the caliphate is established by their contract and choice. If they cannot ascertain that in reality, then attaching the ruling to it would have no benefit, unlike prophethood, for Allah the Exalted is the One who chooses whom He wills from His servants for His message and prophethood, and He is the Knower of the reality of everything. Thus, whomever He chooses from among the people of his time for His message and the bearing of His trust is the most excellent of His creation and the most perfect of His creatures in his time. But in our case, the matter is otherwise. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is a proof (ḥujja) from the Hanafi/Maturidi school refuting the condition that the imam must be the most excellent (afḍal). The argument begins with a historical precedent: when ‘Umar was assassinated, he appointed a consultation committee (shūrā) of six, including both the most excellent and others, without designating the most excellent. The rationale is that the general benefit (maṣlaḥa) and administrative capability are prioritized over personal virtue. The text then argues that true superiority is known only to Allah through hidden matters, so if imamate were conditional on that, it would be impossible for the community to determine. The caliphate is established by human choice, not divine designation like prophethood, where Allah directly chooses the most excellent. Therefore, the imam need not be the most excellent.

Key Terms
أفضلية (afḍaliyya)
شورى (shūrā)
مصلحة (maṣlaḥa)
اجتهاد (ijtihād)
إمامة (imāma)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the imam must be the most excellent in all virtues.
Correction: This proof shows that practical capability for leadership and general benefit take precedence over personal virtue.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi proof, why did ‘Umar not appoint the most excellent among the six for the shūrā?
A) Because the most excellent cannot be identified.
B) Because the most excellent refused the position.
C) Because the choice was based on who would be most beneficial for the community.
D) Because the most excellent were not from Quraysh.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school argues that the imam need not be the most excellent; rather, practical benefit and capability for leadership are the decisive criteria.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If leadership is about benefit and capability, not personal virtue, what does that say about your own ambitions for influence? Are you more concerned with appearing righteous or with being effective?
?
The passage says true superiority is known only to Allah. Does this humble your judgments of others' worth in your community? Who have you dismissed as less worthy while ignoring their practical contributions?
?
The shura after ‘Umar prioritized general benefit over personal excellence. In your family, workplace, or masjid, do you advocate for the most capable leader even if someone more 'pious' is available? What holds you back?

Infallibility Is Not Required for the Imam
Refuting the condition that the imam must be infallible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi school holds that infallibility (ʿiṣma) is a condition for prophethood alone and not for the imam, based on rational and scriptural arguments.

Core Idea
Infallibility is for prophets, proven by miracles; imams need only be just, not infallible.

Sanusi argues that requiring infallibility for the imam is both impractical and unreasonable. In this passage, he explains that infallibility belongs to prophets because their truthfulness is confirmed by miracles. For imams, there is no such divine confirmation, and demanding it would impose an obligation beyond human capacity—a principle rejected by both the Quran and sound reason.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the contrast the author draws between prophets and imams.
2
Identify the main claim
The passage states clearly that infallibility is not a condition for the imam according to the Maturidi school. Look for where this claim is asserted.
The claim appears near the beginning: 'وكذا كونه معصوماً ليس بشرط عندنا'.
3
Follow the argument's logic
The author gives reasons: (1) infallibility is attached to prophethood because of miracles; (2) imams lack such proofs; (3) requiring it without evidence would be an impossible burden (taklīf mā lā yuṭāq). Trace how each reason supports the main claim.
Look for the Quranic citation that reinforces the point.
4
Contrast with prophethood
The passage then contrasts the imam with the Prophet: the Prophet must be infallible because he conveys divine revelation; otherwise, his transmission would be unreliable. Understand why this necessity does not apply to the imam.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this argument is important for the Maturidi position on leadership. It shows that the imam is chosen by human agreement and is not a divinely appointed figure.
This relates to broader discussions about the caliphate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا كونه معصوماً ليس بشرط عندنا بل العصمة من شرط النبوة إذ هي مقترنة بأعلام ومعجزات خارجات عن العادات والطبائع يعرف بذلك صدقهم وتظهر عصمتهم، وليس الأئمة شيء من ذلك، فلو وجب القول بعصمته لوجب من غير دليل، إذ لا عصمة بدون صحة السريرة وسلامة الباطن، ولا وقوف على ذلك إلا بالوحي، ولا وحي مع من يختار الإمام لعقد الإمامة وهم مأمورون بنصب الإمام على ما بينا، فلو لزمهم نصب الإمام المعصوم وليس معهم دليل عصمته فكان فيه تكليف ما ليس في الوسع، والله تعالى تبرأ عن تكليف مثله بقوله تعالى: {لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا} وقبح ذلك أيضا في العقول، على أن النبي عليه السلام يأتي بما هو غائب عن أهل الأرض، وهو الشريعة التي أتى بها وبه ظهور ذلك، ثم يظهر ذلك فيهم بالقول تارة وبالفعل أخرى، فلو لم يكن معصوما لكذب في تبليغه أو نسق في تعاطيه، فتقبل الناس قوله بإباحة شيء هو محرم في الحقيقة إلا أنه كاذب في تبليغه إباحته، وكذا
And likewise, his being infallible is not a condition according to us; rather, infallibility is a condition of prophethood, since it is accompanied by signs and miracles that are outside of custom and nature, by which their truthfulness is known and their infallibility becomes apparent. The imams have none of that. So if it were necessary to hold that he is infallible, it would be necessary without evidence, since there is no infallibility without integrity of the inner self and soundness of the hidden, and there is no access to that except through revelation, and there is no revelation for those who choose the imam for the contract of imamate, and they are commanded to appoint the imam as we have explained. So if they were obligated to appoint an infallible imam while they have no proof of his infallibility, that would be a charge of what is not within capacity, and Allah the Exalted has declared Himself free from such a charge in His saying: "Allah does not charge a soul except [within] its capacity." And that is also considered objectionable in intellects. Moreover, the Prophet - peace be upon him - brings what is absent from the people of the earth, namely the Sharia that he brought, and through him that appears, and then he makes it appear to them sometimes by speech and sometimes by action. So if he were not infallible, he could lie in his conveyance or make a mistake in his conduct, and then the people would accept his statement permitting something that is in reality forbidden while he is lying in his conveyance of its permission. And likewise...
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the imam need not be infallible (ma‘ṣūm). It begins by stating that infallibility is a condition of prophethood, not imamate, because prophets are supported by miracles that prove their truthfulness. For imams, there is no such evidence. If infallibility were required, it would be an obligation without proof, since inner integrity is unknowable without revelation. The community is commanded to appoint an imam, but they cannot determine infallibility. This would be an impossible burden (taklīf mā lā yuṭāq), which is negated by the Quranic verse. Reason also rejects it. The argument contrasts with the Prophet: his infallibility is necessary because he conveys revelation from Allah; without it, his transmission could be unreliable. Therefore, imams, who are chosen by humans, cannot be required to be infallible.

Key Terms
عصمة (ʿiṣma)
معجزة (muʿjiza)
تكليف ما لا يطاق (taklīf mā lā yuṭāq)
وحي (waḥy)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The imam must be infallible to ensure correct leadership.
Correction: The text argues that infallibility is only knowable through revelation and miracles, which imams do not possess; thus requiring it is impractical and imposible.

Checkpoint
Why cannot infallibility be a condition for the imam according to this passage?
A) Because infallibility is impossible for humans.
B) Because there is no way to verify infallibility without revelation, and imams are chosen by humans.
C) Because the imam is always a prophet.
D) Because infallibility is only for angels.

Key Takeaway
Infallibility is a necessary condition for prophets due to miracles and revelation, but it cannot be required for imams because it is unverifiable and would impose an impossible obligation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to choose a leader today, would you demand perfection from them? The passage shows that requiring infallibility is an impossible burden. What do you actually look for in a leader, and does your standard align with what Allah requires from an imam?
?
The passage says inner integrity is unknowable without revelation. How often do you judge others' sincerity without evidence? Think of a time you assumed someone's motives unfairly. How can you apply the lesson's principle to be more just in your assessments?
?
The Prophet's infallibility was proven by miracles that you have not seen. Do you truly trust his words as absolute truth? Ask yourself: which of the Prophet's commands do you find hardest to follow, and what does that reveal about your heart's commitment to the one who is truly infallible?

Why Infallibility Is Not Required for the Imam
Refutation of the condition of infallibility for the imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why infallibility ('isma) is a condition only for prophets, not for imams, based on the distinction between prophetic revelation and the imam's role in implementing revealed law.

Core Idea
Infallibility is only possible through revelation; imams are not prophets, so it cannot be required.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi refutes the Shi'a position that the imam must be infallible. The author systematically argues that infallibility is uniquely linked to prophethood, which is proven by miracles and revelation. Since imams do not bring new revelation and their actions are judged by the same criteria as any Muslim, requiring infallibility would impose an impossible obligation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation to get the overall flow. Notice the clear thesis statement at the beginning.
The author states his position directly: infallibility is not a condition for the imam.
2
Identify the core argument
The author argues that infallibility is for prophets because it is proven by miracles and revelation. Find where he explains this connection.
Look for the phrase 'because infallibility is for prophets' and the mention of 'signs and miracles'.
3
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
The author shows that if infallibility were required for the imam, it would be unprovable and thus an unfair burden, citing the Quranic verse about not burdening beyond capacity.
This logical step strengthens the refutation.
4
Distinguish between prophets and imams
Prophets bring new, unseen revelation; imams only apply what is already known. Understand why this difference makes infallibility unnecessary for imams.
The imam's errors can be corrected by the same means as any other scholar's.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that stipulating infallibility is meaningless. Consider why this argument is sufficient for the intended audience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يشترط عصمة الإمام لأن العصمة للأنبياء. وكذا كونه معصوماً ليس بشرط عندنا بل العصمة من شرط النبوة إذ هي مقترنة بأعلام، ومعجزات خارجات عن العادات والطبائع يعرف بذلك صدقهم وتظهر عصمتهم، وليس الأئمة شيء من ذلك، فلو وجب القول بعصمته لوجب مع من غير دليل، إذ لا عصمة بدون صحة السريرة وسلامة الباطن، ولا وقوف على ذلك إلا بالوحي، ولا وحي مع من يختار الإمام لعقد الإمامة وهم مأمورون بنصب الإمام على ما بينا، فلو لزمهم نصب الإمام المعصوم وليس معهم دليل عصمته فكان فيه تكليف ما ليس في الوسع، والله تعالى تبرأ عن تكليف مثله بقوله تعالى: ﴿ لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا ﴾ ﴿ إِلَّا مَا ءَاتَنها ﴾ وغير ذلك، وقبح ذلك أيضا في العقول، على أن النبي عليه السلام يأتي بما هو غائب عن أهل الأرض، وهو الشريعة التي أتى بها وبه ظهور ذلك، ثم يظهر ذلك فيهم بالقول تارة وبالفعل أخرى، فلو لم يكن معصوما لكذب في تبليغه أو نسق في تعاطيه، فتقبل الناس قوله بإباحة شيء هو محرم في الحقيقة إلا أنه كاذب في تبليغه إباحته، وكذا اعتقدوا إباحة ما عاينوه يتعاطى بناء للأمر على رسالته الثابتة بإعلامه ومعجزاته وذلك في الحقيقة محظور لا مباح فيقع في الناس في الضلال، واعتقاد إباحة ما هو حرام بناء للأمر على المعجزات فتكون المعجزة التي أقامها الله تعالى حجة للرسول موقعة للناس في الكفر والضلال فلابد من ثبوت العصمة لرسول لئلا يؤدي إلى ذلك المحال. فأما الأئمة فما جاءوا بأمر غائب عن أهل الأرض بل هم أمروا بالعمل بما جاء به الرسول عليه السلام من القرآن وغيره، وذلك ظاهر فيما بين الناس، وقد قام بمعرفة ذلك كله علماء الأمة وإنما الإمام للعمل بذلك والحكم به فيما بين الخلق وهو كسائر الأمة في العمل بذلك يظهر صوابه وخطأه بما به يظهر صواب غيره وخطأه، فلا معنى لاشتراط عصمته. وقد بينا بطلان القول بعصمة الإمام في كتابنا المصنف في الرد على الباطنية المترجم بكتاب الإفساد لخدع أهل الإلحاد - بما فيه كفاية وفيما ذكرنا لها هنا مقنع.
The infallibility of the imam is not a condition, because infallibility is for prophets. And likewise his being infallible is not a condition in our view; rather infallibility is a condition of prophethood, since it is coupled with signs and miracles outside of habits and natures, by which their truthfulness is known and their infallibility appears. And the imams have none of that. So if the statement of his infallibility were obligatory, it would be obligatory without proof, since there is no infallibility without soundness of conscience and integrity of inner being, and there is no knowledge of that except through revelation, and there is no revelation with those who choose the imam for the contract of imamate, while they are commanded to appoint the imam as we have explained. So if they were obliged to appoint the infallible imam while they have no proof of his infallibility, that would involve an obligation beyond capacity, and Allah Almighty has disassociated Himself from such obligation by His saying: "Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity" and "except what He has given it," and other [verses], and that is also considered ugly by intellects. Moreover, the prophet, peace be upon him, brings what is absent from the people of the earth, that is the Sharia which he brought and through him it appears, then he manifests it among them sometimes by speech and sometimes by action. So if he were not infallible, he would lie in his conveyance or err in his practice, so people would accept his statement permitting something that is actually forbidden, while he is lying in his conveyance of its permissibility. And likewise they would believe in the permissibility of what they see him practicing based on his mission established by his signs and miracles, while it is actually prohibited, not permissible, so the people would fall into error. And believing in the permissibility of what is forbidden based on miracles would make the miracle that Allah established as a proof for the messenger become a cause for people's unbelief and error. Therefore, the infallibility of the messenger must be established lest that absurdity occur. As for the imams, they have not brought any matter absent from the people of the earth; rather they are commanded to act by what the messenger brought of the Qur'an and other things, and that is apparent among the people. The scholars of the ummah have taken up knowledge of all that. The imam is only to act by that and judge by it among creation, and he is like the rest of the ummah in acting by that; his rightness and error appear by the same means as the rightness and error of others appear. So there is no meaning to stipulating his infallibility. And we have already explained the invalidity of the statement of the imam's infallibility in our work composed in refutation of the Batiniyya, titled 'The Book of Corruption of the Deceptions of the People of Heresy' — sufficient therein, and what we have mentioned here is convincing.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Shi'a condition that the imam must be infallible (ma'sum). The author begins by stating categorically that infallibility is not required for the imam, because it is a condition specific to prophets. He then explains why prophethood requires infallibility: prophets bring unseen revelation and perform miracles that exceed natural laws, and their truthfulness is established through these miracles. Imams, by contrast, have no such miracles. If infallibility were required for the imam, it would have to be proven without evidence, since infallibility can only be known through revelation, yet revelation is not given to those who elect the imam. This would impose an obligation beyond human capacity, which God's verse ('Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity') and sound reason reject. The author then elaborates on the necessity of infallibility for prophets: without it, people could be misled into believing that a forbidden act is permissible based on the prophet's actions or statements, and the prophet's miracle could become a cause for disbelief. This is an impossible outcome, so infallibility is essential for prophets. In contrast, imams only deal with the already-revealed Sharia, which is known to the ulema; the imam's errors can be corrected by the same means as any other person's, so stipulating his infallibility is meaningless. The author concludes by referencing his own book refuting the Batiniyya, which contains a fuller argument, but states that what he has said here is sufficient.

Key Terms
عصمة
نبوة
إمامة
معجزات
تكليف
وسع
شرط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the imam must be infallible (ma'sum) like a prophet.
Correction: The author argues that infallibility is only known through revelation and miracles, which apply exclusively to prophets. Imams do not receive revelation nor perform miracles, so requiring infallibility is both impossible and unnecessary.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that infallibility cannot be a condition for the imam?
A) Because infallibility is only known through revelation and imams do not receive revelation.
B) Because the imam is chosen by the people, not by God.
C) Because the imam is not required to perform miracles.
D) Because the imam is a sinner like all humans.

Key Takeaway
The imam's lack of infallibility does not undermine his authority because he only executes the revealed law, not adding to it, and his errors can be corrected by normal scholarly scrutiny.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage argues that requiring infallibility for the imam would be 'an obligation beyond capacity,' which Allah does not command. In your own life, have you imposed extra obligations on yourself or others that Allah never required? What would it take for you to release those burdens today?
?
Think of a religious teacher, leader, or influencer you trust implicitly. Do you treat their words as if they were infallible, even when they contradict clear evidence from the Quran and Sunnah? How can you train yourself to evaluate their teachings with the same standard you would apply to anyone else, without falling into blind following?
?
If you were to make a mistake in teaching or practicing Islam, would you be open to correction from others? The author says the imam's 'rightness and error appear by the same means as the rightness and error of others appear.' When was the last time you gratefully accepted correction in a matter of religion? What prevents you from doing so more readily?

Imamate: Choice or Inheritance?
The author states that imamate is confirmed by the choice of righteous people, not by inheritance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Sunni position on imamate is that it is established by the choice of righteous and just individuals, not by inheritance, and that this is supported by the consensus on Abu Bakr's caliphate.

Core Idea
Imamate is by selection, not inheritance.

This lesson presents a foundational Sunni belief about how leadership (imamate) is established. The author contrasts the Sunni view with that of those who believe in hereditary succession, grounding his argument in the historical consensus on Abu Bakr's caliphate. Following this passage, you'll see how the author defends the legitimacy of the first caliph.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style; this is a doctrinal statement.
2
Identify the two sides: choice vs inheritance
The passage presents two methods of establishing imamate: by choice (اختيار) and by inheritance (وراثة). Mark which one the author affirms and which he rejects.
The author explicitly rejects inheritance.
3
Understand the evidence: consensus on Abu Bakr
The author cites the consensus of Sunni scholars on the validity of Abu Bakr's imamate. This serves as proof that imamate is established by choice, not inheritance.
Ask: Why does this consensus support the chosen view?
4
Reflect on the implication
Think about what this refutes: the Shi'a belief in appointment by inheritance or divine designation. The Sunni view emphasizes communal selection.
This is a key point of difference between Sunni and Shi'a theology.
5
Connect to broader Aqeedah
Consider how imamate fits into Sunni creed: it is not a matter of divine appointment but of community consensus and qualification.
This lesson is part of a larger discussion on leadership.

Source Text

ثم الإمامة عندنا تثبت باختيار أهل العدالة والصلاح لا بالوراثة. وإليه ذهب جميع من قال من علماء الأمة بصحة إمامة أبي بكر له.
Then the imamate, in our view, is established by the choice of the people of justice and righteousness, not by inheritance. And to this went all who spoke from the scholars of the ummah regarding the validity of the imamate of Abu Bakr for him.

Commentary
This passage is a concise doctrinal statement on the method of establishing the imamate. The author asserts that the imamate is confirmed through the selection of upright and just individuals (ahl al-‘adala wa al-salah), not through hereditary succession. He then cites the consensus of Sunni scholars on the legitimacy of Abu Bakr's caliphate as evidence. This refutes the Shi'a belief in appointment by inheritance or divine designation. The unfinished phrase about al-Rawandiyya introduces a sect that held a different view, but the lesson stops here.

Refuting Inheritance and Nass-Based Imamate Claims
The author reports and refutes three sectarian theories of imamate by inheritance or nass.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various sectarian claims that the imamate is established by inheritance or explicit designation (nass), and the logical arguments the author uses to refute them.

Core Idea
Inheritance and nass cannot establish imamate; priority and consistency disprove both.

In this passage, the author reports the views of the Rawandiyya, Jārūdiyya, and Imāmiyya sects, who assert that the imamate passes through inheritance or by a specific text from the Prophet. He then systematically refutes these claims using simple principles of inheritance law and logical consistency. This lesson unpacks both the reported claims and the refutation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sectarian views
Read the passage and list the three groups mentioned: Rawandiyya (with two sub-views), Jārūdiyya, and Imāmiyya. Note each group's specific claim about how the imamate is transmitted.
The Rawandiyya split on inheritance vs nass; the Jārūdiyya combine nass by description and inheritance in the Husaynid line; the Imāmiyya hold pure inheritance.
2
Understand the inheritance argument
The author argues that if imamate were by inheritance, al-‘Abbās (the uncle) would be more entitled than ‘Alī (the cousin). Understand why this is a valid objection using standard Islamic inheritance rules where the uncle takes precedence.
3
Analyze the naṣṣ argument
The author shows that the claim of designation by naṣṣ is forced and logically inconsistent because inheritance cannot be overridden by a mere statement. Consider the reasoning that a testator cannot deprive an heir by saying the inheritance belongs to another.
4
Reflect on the promised demonstration
The author concludes by promising a fuller proof from consensus (ijmā‘) on Abū Bakr’s caliphate. Think about how ijmā‘ would refute both inheritance and nass theories.
This final point is not detailed here but sets up the next discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القائلة بإمامة العباس وهم أتباع القاسم بن راوند فيختلفون فمنهم من زعم أن الإمامة تثبت بالوراثة وبها استحقها العباس رضي الله عنه، ومنهم من زعم أنه استحقها بنص النبي عليه السلام لا بالوراثة، وزعمت الجارودية من الروافض، وهم من جملة الزيدية أن النبي عليه السلام نص على خلافة علي رضي الله عنه بالوصف دون الاسم ثم ورثها من علي ابناه الحسن والحسين ثم إنهما على الميراث في هذين البطنين لا لواحد بعينه، ولكن من خرج منهم شاهرا سيفه يدعو إلى سبيل ربه وكان عالمًا صالحًا فهو الإمام، وزعم أكثر الإمامية أن الإمامة موروثة، وهذا خطأ، لأنها لو كانت بالوراثة لكان العباس أولى من علي رضي الله عنهما لأن العم أولى بالميراث من ابن العم وزعمهم أن عليا استحقه بالنص اضطرارًا لئلا يلزمهم هذا باطل، إذ لو كانت تستحق بالوراثة لما بطلت بالنص، ولا يحرم الوارث عن الميراث بنص الموروث أن الميراث لغيره، ثم لو كانت بالوراثة لما كان ينبغي أن يكون الحسن أولى بها من الحسين - رضي الله عنهما - ولما كان ينبغي أن ينتقل عن الحسن إلى الحسين مع وجود الأبناء للحسن، ثم نبين بعد هذا إبطال ثبوت الخلافة بالنص وانعقاد الإجماع على خلافة الصديق يظهر بطلان القول بكونها مستحقة بالوراثة أو النص، والله الموفق.
Those who say the imamate belongs to al-‘Abbās are the followers of al-Qāsim b. Rāwand. They differ: some claim that the imamate is established by inheritance, and by it al-‘Abbās deserved it, may God be pleased with him; and some claim that he deserved it by the text (naṣṣ) of the Prophet, peace be upon him, not by inheritance. The Jārūdiyya of the Rāfiḍa, who are among the Zaydiyya, claimed that the Prophet, peace be upon him, designated ‘Alī, may God be pleased with him, for the caliphate by description without naming him, then his sons al-Ḥasan and al-Ḥusayn inherited it from ‘Alī; then the inheritance is confined to these two lines, not to a particular individual, but whoever among them comes out unsheathing his sword calling to the way of his Lord and is knowledgeable and righteous is the imam. Most of the Imāmiyya claimed that the imamate is inherited. This is a mistake, because if it were by inheritance, then al-‘Abbās would be more entitled than ‘Alī, may God be pleased with them both, for the paternal uncle is more entitled to inheritance than the cousin. Their claim that ‘Alī deserved it by the naṣṣ is forced to avoid this [contradiction], but it is false, because if it were deserved by inheritance, it would not be invalidated by naṣṣ, and the heir is not deprived of inheritance by the testator's statement that the inheritance belongs to someone else. Moreover, if it were by inheritance, it would not be appropriate for al-Ḥasan to be more entitled than al-Ḥusayn, may God be pleased with them both, and it would not be appropriate for it to pass from al-Ḥasan to al-Ḥusayn while al-Ḥasan had sons. Then we will show after this the invalidation of establishing the caliphate by naṣṣ and the occurrence of consensus on the caliphate of al-Ṣiddīq, which will make clear the falsehood of the claim that it is deserved by inheritance or naṣṣ. God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage is a doxographical report followed by a refutation. The author first describes three sectarian views: (1) the Rawandiyya, followers of al-Qāsim b. Rāwand, who split between those who say the imamate is inherited by al-‘Abbās and those who say it is by explicit text (naṣṣ) from the Prophet; (2) the Jārūdiyya, a sub-sect of the Zaydiyya, who claim that the Prophet designated ‘Alī by description (waṣf) without naming him, and thereafter the imamate is inherited in the lines of al-Ḥasan and al-Ḥusayn, with the condition that the imam must be a learned, righteous man who rises with the sword; (3) the majority of the Imāmiyya, who hold that the imamate is inherited. The author then refutes these views with logical arguments. First, if the imamate were by inheritance, then al-‘Abbās (the Prophet’s uncle) would be more entitled than ‘Alī (the Prophet’s cousin), since the uncle takes precedence in inheritance. The Jārūdiyya’s claim that ‘Alī was designated by naṣṣ is a forced attempt to avoid this implication, but it fails because inheritance cannot be nullified by a mere statement. Second, if it were by inheritance, al-Ḥasan should not have been more entitled than al-Ḥusayn, and the imamate should not have passed from al-Ḥasan to al-Ḥusayn while al-Ḥasan had sons. The author concludes by promising a fuller demonstration later that the caliphate was not established by naṣṣ and that consensus (ijmā‘) on Abū Bakr’s caliphate proves the falsehood of both inheritance and naṣṣ theories.

Key Terms
الإمامة (imāma)
الوراثة (al-wirātha)
النص (al-naṣṣ)
الروافض (al-rawāfiḍ)
الزيدية (al-zaydiyya)
الجارودية (al-jārūdiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the author supports the idea that the imamate can be inherited or established by nass.
Correction: The author explicitly refutes both inheritance and nass-based claims, showing logical contradictions and promising a consensus-based refutation.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the claim that ‘Alī deserved the imamate by inheritance contradictory?
A) Because the Prophet did not have a son.
B) Because al-‘Abbās, as the Prophet's uncle, would be more entitled than ‘Alī, the cousin.
C) Because the Jārūdiyya denied inheritance altogether.
D) Because the Imāmiyya rejected the caliphate.

Key Takeaway
The author refutes inheritance and nass theories of imamate by showing logical contradictions in priority and consistency, and promises a consensus-based refutation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own religious convictions, do you ever assume that truth or authority runs in your family line? In what ways might you be subtly relying on inherited beliefs rather than personally verifying them through the consensus of the community and sound reasoning? Will you commit to examining at least one inherited belief this week using the same logical scrutiny the author applies to these sectarian claims?
?
The author uses stark logical contradictions to dismantle the inheritance theory. Are there any beliefs you hold that cannot withstand logical scrutiny? What would it cost you to admit that a cherished belief is unsound, and are you willing to pay that price for the sake of truth?
?
If the caliphate was established by consensus (ijma'), not inheritance or nass, how does that affect your understanding of legitimate religious authority today? Do you tend to follow individuals or families because of their lineage rather than their adherence to the truth and the consensus of the community? Confront that tendency in yourself and decide to change.

The Sunni Position and First Proof Against Nass
Sanusi states the Sunni method of imamate and presents the first rational proof against nass.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni method of establishing the imamate through ijtihad and the first rational proof that no explicit text (nass) exists because the caliphate is a matter of universal concern that would be widely known if divinely designated.

Core Idea
If nass existed for the caliphate, it would be as well-known as the qibla.

The author begins by asserting the Sunni position that the imamate is established through ijtihad and consultation, not by explicit divine text. He then refutes the claims of the Rafidah and Rawandiyyah by presenting a key proof: matters of universal necessity, like the caliphate, would have a universally known nass if it existed. The absence of such a report proves there is no nass.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage twice
First read the Arabic and translation to get the gist. Then read again, focusing on the logical structure.
Notice the initial statement of the Sunni method followed by the refutation.
2
Identify the two sects and their claims
The passage mentions the Rafidah (who claim nass for Ali) and the Rawandiyyah (who claim nass for al-Abbas). Understand that the author rejects both.
3
Understand the qibla analogy
The author argues that if nass existed for a universal matter like the caliphate, it would be as widely known as the nass on the qibla, prayer rak'ahs, and zakat obligations. Since no such widespread report exists, there is no nass.
This is the core of the first proof.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that there is absolutely no nass in this matter. Ask yourself why this proof is considered strong in Islamic theology.
Think about the principle that divine guidance for communal matters must be clear and accessible.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم طريق ثبوت الإمامة لمن يصلح أهلاً لها على سبيل الاجتهاد واستعمال الرأي على ما يستعمل في الحوادث الشرعية التي بالناس إلى معرفة أحكامها حاجة وقد عدموا فيها النص إذ لا نص ها هنا، وقول الروافض بوجود النص من النبي عليه السلام على علي عليه السلام وقول الراوندية بوجود النص على العباس رضي الله عنه باطل. رد القول بالنص في الإمامة والدليل على بطلان النص أن أمر الخلافة أمر عام يقع بكل الناس إلى معرفته حاجة ماسة، وما هذا سبيله كان النص فيه لو كان ثابتا يشتهر اشتهارا لا يبقى معه على أحد من الناس خفاء، ولا اضطر الناس إلى معرفته كالنص على القبلة وعلى أعداد ركعات الصلاة ومقاديرها وأوقاتها ومقادير النصيب والواجبات في باب الزكاة، وغير ذلك من الأمور العامة، ولما لم يوجد في ذلك خبر هذا سبيله، دل أن لا نص فيه البتة، يدل عليه أن النص لو كان ثابتا لما أعرضت الصحابة مع جلالة أقدارهم في الدين وشدة ورعهم وتمسكهم بالدين وتحرزهم عن مخالفة الشريعة عن قبوله والعمل به وتفويض الأمر إلى المنصوص عليه، بل بادروا إليه وولوه الأمر ولم ينازعه أحد في ذلك إذ لم يكن تقلد من تقلد للأمر منهم رغبة في الجاه والمنزلة والترأس ولا حرصا على جمع الحطام والاستمتاع باللذات البدنية والشهوات الطبيعية بل كان تقلدهم لذلك للقيام بحقوق الدين واستيفاء حقوق الله تعالى وتقوية الملة والسعى في إعلاء كلمة الله تعالى وقهر أعدائه وتشييد بنيان الإسلام ألا ترى الصديق رضي الله عنه كيف كانت معاملته الخلق ورفضه الشهوات والاكتفاء باليسير من القوت والخشن من الثياب والاجتزاء بقليل من بيت المال، ثم الأمر برد ذلك عند وفاته إلى بيت المال، وكذا عمر رضي الله عنه، وكذا الخليفتان بعدهما - رضي الله عنهما - وإذا كان تقلدهم لما ذكر فكيف يظن بواحد منهم الإعراض عن قبول النص الثابت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والتمسك بمخالفته؟!، ولو أن واحدا منهم ضل عن رشده وزاغ عن الهدى وآثر مخالفة الرسول عليه السلام، ولم يبال من مقت الله تعالى رغبة منه في استجماع الحطام والاسكثار من الحرام لما جبل عليه من شدة النفس وشؤم الطبع، كيف ساعده على ذلك نجباء الصحابة وكبار المهاجرين والأنصار وعلماء الأمة، وخيار الخليفة الذين شهد الله تعالى لهم بكونهم خير أمة وجعلهم أمة وسطا ليكونوا شهداء على الناس؟! ثم كيف امتنعوا عن الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن هذا المنكر الذي هو مخالفة رسول الله عليه السلام وغصب الأمر أهله، والقيام بتنفيذ الأحكام في الدماء والفروج و الأموال من غير ثبوت الولاية مع أن الله تعالى وصفهم بالأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر، ومدحهم على ذلك وأثنى به عليهم، أفترى الله تعالى لم يعلم بما يوجد منهم بعد وفاة النبي عليه السلام من تقاعدهم عن الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر، وتسارعهم إلى إعانة المبطل وخذلان المحق حتى وصفهم الله تعالى بذلك وأثنى عليهم به؟! وهذا والله هو الظن المحال والرأي الفاسد والقول الباطل. ثم كيف يظن مسلم أن رهط اختارهم الله تعالى لنصرة رسوله الذي هو خير البشر وصفوة الأنام وخيرته من خلقه، واصطفاهم لصحبته، وأسعدهم بقربه
Then the method of establishing the imamate for one who is qualified for it is by way of ijtihad and the use of opinion, as is done in the legal incidents which people need to know their rulings, and they have no text (nass) therein, for there is no text here. And the saying of the Rafidah that there is a text from the Prophet, peace be upon him, for Ali, peace be upon him, and the saying of the Rawandiyyah that there is a text for al-Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, is false. Refutation of the claim of text (nass) in the imamate. And the proof of the invalidity of nass is that the matter of the caliphate is a general matter which all people have an urgent need to know. And whatever is of this nature, if nass were established in it, it would become widely known in such a way that no one would remain in ignorance of it, and people would not be in confusion about it, like the nass on the qibla, and on the numbers of rak'ahs of prayer, their measures and times, and the measures of shares and obligations in the chapter of zakat, and other general matters. And since there has not come in that any report of this nature, it indicates that there is absolutely no nass in it. And it is further indicated by the fact that if nass were established, the Companions, despite the greatness of their status in religion, their severe piety, their adherence to religion, and their caution against violating the Sharia, would not have turned away from accepting it and acting upon it and entrusting the matter to the designated person. Rather, they would have hastened to him and given him authority, and no one would have disputed him in that, since whoever assumed authority among them did so not out of desire for position, status, and leadership, nor out of eagerness to amass worldly goods and enjoy physical pleasures and natural desires, but rather their assumption of authority was for the sake of fulfilling the rights of religion, exacting the rights of Allah Almighty, strengthening the religious community, striving to elevate the word of Allah Almighty, and defeating His enemies and strengthening the edifice of Islam. Do you not see how al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him, dealt with people, rejected pleasures, contented himself with little sustenance and coarse clothing, and sufficed with little from the treasury, and then ordered its return to the treasury upon his death? And likewise Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, and likewise the two caliphs after them, may Allah be pleased with them both. And if their assumption of authority was as mentioned, then how could it be thought of any one of them that he would turn away from accepting the established nass from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and adhere to opposing it?! And if any one of them had strayed from his right guidance, deviated from guidance, preferred opposing the Messenger, peace be upon him, and did not care about the wrath of Allah Almighty, out of desire to amass worldly goods and seek abundance of forbidden things due to the severity of his soul and the ill nature with which he was created, how could the noble Companions, the senior Muhajirun and Ansar, and the scholars of the community, and the best of the caliphs, whom Allah Almighty testified to be the best community and made them a middle community to be witnesses over people, have assisted him in that? Then how could they have refrained from enjoining good and forbidding this evil, which is opposing the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and usurping the matter from its rightful people, and from executing legal rulings regarding blood, private parts, and wealth without established authority, while Allah Almighty described them as enjoining good and forbidding evil, praised them for that, and commended them for it? Do you think that Allah Almighty did not know what would occur from them after the death of the Prophet, peace be upon him, of their reluctance to enjoin good and forbid evil, and their hastening to help the false and abandon the true, such that He described them with that and praised them for it?! This, by Allah, is an impossible supposition, a corrupt opinion, and a false statement. Then how can a Muslim think that a group whom Allah Almighty chose to support His Messenger, who is the best of mankind, the chosen of creation, and the elect of His creatures, and whom He selected for his companionship, and made fortunate by his proximity.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim of the Rafidah and Rawandiyyah that the caliphate was explicitly designated (nass) by the Prophet. The author first notes the Sunni position that the imamate is established through ijtihad and consultation, as no explicit text exists. He then presents a two-part proof. First, the imamate is a matter of universal concern; if there were an explicit text, it would be as well-known as the qibla or prayer rak'ahs. Since no such widespread report exists, there is no nass. Second, if a nass existed, the pious Companions would not have ignored it. The author elaborates on the impeccable character of Abu Bakr, Umar, and others, arguing that their asceticism and dedication to truth make it inconceivable that they would suppress a divine designation. He further argues that the other Companions, who were praised by Allah for enjoining good and forbidding evil, would have corrected any such usurpation. The passage concludes by dismissing the opposing view as impossible and corrupt.

Key Terms
النص (nass)
الإمامة (imamate)
الاجتهاد (ijtihad)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that an explicit divine text exists naming the caliph, but it was suppressed or hidden.
Correction: The author argues that a matter so vital would be as widely known as the qibla; its absence shows no such text exists.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the absence of a widespread report about the caliphate indicate there is no nass?
A) The Companions were not trustworthy.
B) The caliphate is a matter of universal concern, so any nass would be widely known like the qibla.
C) The nass was only for the Prophet himself.
D) The caliphate was never important.

Key Takeaway
The absence of widespread knowledge of a nass for the caliphate proves that no explicit divine text exists.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage argues that truly universal religious matters are made known to all. Think of a belief you hold that you consider absolutely essential. Have you ever verified whether it is based on clear, widely-known evidence, or are you simply following what you grew up with? Will you commit to seeking the source of that belief today?
?
The Rafidah and Rawandiyyah insisted on a nass that does not exist. Are there any 'nasses' you hold onto—beliefs you treat as divinely mandated—that actually lack solid evidence? Would you be willing to subject them to the same logical test this passage uses? If you find yourself resisting, what does that say about your attachment to those beliefs?
?
If the caliphate had a nass, you would be expected to accept it unquestioningly. Would you? Or would you demand evidence? Now consider: in your own life, when you face a major decision, do you seek clear guidance from Allah (like a 'nass') or do you use reasoning and consultation? Which approach does this passage encourage, and how will you apply it to a current choice?

The Second Proof: The Piety of the Companions
Sanusi presents the second rational argument against nass based on the Companions' moral integrity and the community's duty to enjoin good.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second proof against nass: the impeccable character of the Companions, including Abu Bakr and Umar, makes it impossible that they would ignore an explicit divine designation or that the community would accept such a violation.

Core Idea
The Companions' virtue and integrity preclude any conspiracy to hide a nass.

Sanusi continues his refutation with a powerful argument from the character of the Companions. He argues that if a nass existed, the pious Companions would not have turned away from it. He illustrates their asceticism and devotion through the examples of Abu Bakr and Umar, and asks rhetorical questions about the rest of the community, who were praised by Allah for enjoining good and forbidding evil. The conclusion is that believing in a hidden nass is an impossible and corrupt opinion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
This passage is longer. Read it once to get the overall argument, then re-read focusing on the examples.
Pay attention to the descriptions of the caliphs' character.
2
Identify the main argument
The author argues that if nass existed, the Companions would have accepted it due to their piety. He then gives examples.
The argument is a conditional: if nass, then acceptance; but acceptance did not happen, so nass is false.
3
Analyze the example of Abu Bakr and Umar
The author describes Abu Bakr's asceticism: simple food, coarse clothes, returning treasury money upon death. Umar is similar. This shows they were not motivated by worldly gain.
This serves to prove they would not reject a true nass out of desire for power.
4
Consider the rhetorical questions
The author asks how the other Companions, who were praised by Allah for enjoining good and forbidding evil, could remain silent if a nass were suppressed. This is a powerful argument from collective integrity.
It implies that the entire community of Companions, including the scholars, would have corrected any deviation.

ثم طريق ثبوت الإمامة لمن يصلح أهلاً لها على سبيل الاجتهاد واستعمال الرأي على ما يستعمل في الحوادث الشرعية التي بالناس إلى معرفة أحكامها حاجة وقد عدموا فيها النص إذ لا نص ها هنا، وقول الروافض بوجود النص من النبي عليه السلام على علي عليه السلام وقول الراوندية بوجود النص على العباس رضي الله عنه باطل. رد القول بالنص في الإمامة والدليل على بطلان النص أن أمر الخلافة أمر عام يقع بكل الناس إلى معرفته حاجة ماسة، وما هذا سبيله كان النص فيه لو كان ثابتا يشتهر اشتهارا لا يبقى معه على أحد من الناس خفاء، ولا اضطر الناس إلى معرفته كالنص على القبلة وعلى أعداد ركعات الصلاة ومقاديرها وأوقاتها ومقادير النصيب والواجبات في باب الزكاة، وغير ذلك من الأمور العامة، ولما لم يوجد في ذلك خبر هذا سبيله، دل أن لا نص فيه البتة، يدل عليه أن النص لو كان ثابتا لما أعرضت الصحابة مع جلالة أقدارهم في الدين وشدة ورعهم وتمسكهم بالدين وتحرزهم عن مخالفة الشريعة عن قبوله والعمل به وتفويض الأمر إلى المنصوص عليه، بل بادروا إليه وولوه الأمر ولم ينازعه أحد في ذلك إذ لم يكن تقلد من تقلد للأمر منهم رغبة في الجاه والمنزلة والترأس ولا حرصا على جمع الحطام والاستمتاع باللذات البدنية والشهوات الطبيعية بل كان تقلدهم لذلك للقيام بحقوق الدين واستيفاء حقوق الله تعالى وتقوية الملة والسعى في إعلاء كلمة الله تعالى وقهر أعدائه وتشييد بنيان الإسلام ألا ترى الصديق رضي الله عنه كيف كانت معاملته الخلق ورفضه الشهوات والاكتفاء باليسير من القوت والخشن من الثياب والاجتزاء بقليل من بيت المال، ثم الأمر برد ذلك عند وفاته إلى بيت المال، وكذا عمر رضي الله عنه، وكذا الخليفتان بعدهما - رضي الله عنهما - وإذا كان تقلدهم لما ذكر فكيف يظن بواحد منهم الإعراض عن قبول النص الثابت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والتمسك بمخالفته؟!، ولو أن واحدا منهم ضل عن رشده وزاغ عن الهدى وآثر مخالفة الرسول عليه السلام، ولم يبال من مقت الله تعالى رغبة منه في استجماع الحطام والاسكثار من الحرام لما جبل عليه من شدة النفس وشؤم الطبع، كيف ساعده على ذلك نجباء الصحابة وكبار المهاجرين والأنصار وعلماء الأمة، وخيار الخليفة الذين شهد الله تعالى لهم بكونهم خير أمة وجعلهم أمة وسطا ليكونوا شهداء على الناس؟! ثم كيف امتنعوا عن الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن هذا المنكر الذي هو مخالفة رسول الله عليه السلام وغصب الأمر أهله، والقيام بتنفيذ الأحكام في الدماء والفروج و الأموال من غير ثبوت الولاية مع أن الله تعالى وصفهم بالأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر، ومدحهم على ذلك وأثنى به عليهم، أفترى الله تعالى لم يعلم بما يوجد منهم بعد وفاة النبي عليه السلام من تقاعدهم عن الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر، وتسارعهم إلى إعانة المبطل وخذلان المحق حتى وصفهم الله تعالى بذلك وأثنى عليهم به؟! وهذا والله هو الظن المحال والرأي الفاسد والقول الباطل. ثم كيف يظن مسلم أن رهط اختارهم الله تعالى لنصرة رسوله الذي هو خير البشر وصفوة الأنام وخيرته من خلقه، واصطفاهم لصحبته، وأسعدهم بقربه
Then the method of establishing the imamate for one who is qualified for it is by way of ijtihad and the use of opinion, as is done in the legal incidents which people need to know their rulings, and they have no text (nass) therein, for there is no text here. And the saying of the Rafidah that there is a text from the Prophet, peace be upon him, for Ali, peace be upon him, and the saying of the Rawandiyyah that there is a text for al-Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, is false. Refutation of the claim of text (nass) in the imamate. And the proof of the invalidity of nass is that the matter of the caliphate is a general matter which all people have an urgent need to know. And whatever is of this nature, if nass were established in it, it would become widely known in such a way that no one would remain in ignorance of it, and people would not be in confusion about it, like the nass on the qibla, and on the numbers of rak'ahs of prayer, their measures and times, and the measures of shares and obligations in the chapter of zakat, and other general matters. And since there has not come in that any report of this nature, it indicates that there is absolutely no nass in it. And it is further indicated by the fact that if nass were established, the Companions, despite the greatness of their status in religion, their severe piety, their adherence to religion, and their caution against violating the Sharia, would not have turned away from accepting it and acting upon it and entrusting the matter to the designated person. Rather, they would have hastened to him and given him authority, and no one would have disputed him in that, since whoever assumed authority among them did so not out of desire for position, status, and leadership, nor out of eagerness to amass worldly goods and enjoy physical pleasures and natural desires, but rather their assumption of authority was for the sake of fulfilling the rights of religion, exacting the rights of Allah Almighty, strengthening the religious community, striving to elevate the word of Allah Almighty, and defeating His enemies and strengthening the edifice of Islam. Do you not see how al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him, dealt with people, rejected pleasures, contented himself with little sustenance and coarse clothing, and sufficed with little from the treasury, and then ordered its return to the treasury upon his death? And likewise Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, and likewise the two caliphs after them, may Allah be pleased with them both. And if their assumption of authority was as mentioned, then how could it be thought of any one of them that he would turn away from accepting the established nass from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and adhere to opposing it?! And if any one of them had strayed from his right guidance, deviated from guidance, preferred opposing the Messenger, peace be upon him, and did not care about the wrath of Allah Almighty, out of desire to amass worldly goods and seek abundance of forbidden things due to the severity of his soul and the ill nature with which he was created, how could the noble Companions, the senior Muhajirun and Ansar, and the scholars of the community, and the best of the caliphs, whom Allah Almighty testified to be the best community and made them a middle community to be witnesses over people, have assisted him in that? Then how could they have refrained from enjoining good and forbidding this evil, which is opposing the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and usurping the matter from its rightful people, and from executing legal rulings regarding blood, private parts, and wealth without established authority, while Allah Almighty described them as enjoining good and forbidding evil, praised them for that, and commended them for it? Do you think that Allah Almighty did not know what would occur from them after the death of the Prophet, peace be upon him, of their reluctance to enjoin good and forbid evil, and their hastening to help the false and abandon the true, such that He described them with that and praised them for it?! This, by Allah, is an impossible supposition, a corrupt opinion, and a false statement. Then how can a Muslim think that a group whom Allah Almighty chose to support His Messenger, who is the best of mankind, the chosen of creation, and the elect of His creatures, and whom He selected for his companionship, and made fortunate by his proximity.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim of the Rafidah and Rawandiyyah that the caliphate was explicitly designated (nass) by the Prophet. The author first notes the Sunni position that the imamate is established through ijtihad and consultation, as no explicit text exists. He then presents a two-part proof. First, the imamate is a matter of universal concern; if there were an explicit text, it would be as well-known as the qibla or prayer rak'ahs. Since no such widespread report exists, there is no nass. Second, if a nass existed, the pious Companions would not have ignored it. The author elaborates on the impeccable character of Abu Bakr, Umar, and others, arguing that their asceticism and dedication to truth make it inconceivable that they would suppress a divine designation. He further argues that the other Companions, who were praised by Allah for enjoining good and forbidding evil, would have corrected any such usurpation. The passage concludes by dismissing the opposing view as impossible and corrupt.

Key Terms
الصحابة (Companions)
الخلفاء الراشدون (Rightly Guided Caliphs)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that the Companions ignored or suppressed a nass for worldly gain.
Correction: The author proves that the Companions were deeply pious and ascetic, making it impossible for them to ignore a divine text.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do the examples of Abu Bakr and Umar demonstrate?
A) They were wealthy leaders.
B) They were not concerned with religion.
C) They were ascetic and dedicated to religious duty.
D) They were unwilling to lead.

Key Takeaway
The Companions' proven piety and the community's duty to enjoin good make it impossible that a divine nass for the caliphate was ignored or concealed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Companions' actions were not driven by worldly gain. How much of your religious practice is motivated by what others will think rather than by sincerity to Allah? Will you examine your intentions today?
?
If you were in a situation where the truth was inconvenient, would you still uphold it as the Companions did? What would you be willing to sacrifice?
?
The Companions corrected each other. Do you have a relationship where you can enjoin good and forbid evil with humility? When was the last time you did so, or accepted correction from someone?

Sects and Disagreements
