5 min
The Integrity of the Early Caliphs Precludes Rejecting a Nass
Nasafi argues from the caliphs' integrity that they could not have rejected a nass

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi argues that it is inconceivable for the early caliphs to have rejected a textual designation from the Prophet.

Core Idea
The caliphs' known integrity makes it impossible they ignored a nass.

Nasafi opens his refutation by pointing to the financial uprightness of the caliphs. He then poses a rhetorical question: if they were so trustworthy, how could anyone think they would reject an established text from the Prophet? This lesson examines that foundational argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Nasafi uses a series of rhetorical questions.
2
Identify the premise and the rhetorical question
The passage begins with a premise about the caliphs' financial integrity. Then Nasafi asks: if they undertook this, how could they abandon the nass? Identify this core question.
3
Trace the hypothetical argument
Nasafi imagines one caliph straying and then asks how the other Companions would have assisted him. Notice that he uses the community's obligation to enjoin good to close the argument.
This shows that the argument is both rational and based on Islamic principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من بيت المال، ثم الأمر برد ذلك عند وفاته إلى بيت المال، وكذا عمره، وكذا الخليفتان بعدهما - رضي الله عنهما - وإذا كان تقلدهم لما ذكر فكيف يظن بواحد منهم الإعراض عن قبول النص الثابت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والتمسك بمخالفته؟! ولو أن واحدا منهم ضل عن رشده وزاغ عن الهدى وآثر مخالفة الرسول عليه السلام، ولم يبال من مقت الله تعالى رغبة منه في استجماع الحطام والاسكثار من الحرام لما جبل عليه من شدة النفس وشؤم الطبع، كيف ساعده على ذلك نجباء الصحابة وكبار المهاجرين والأنصار وعلماء الأمة، وخيار الخليفة الذين شهد الله تعالى لهم بكونهم خير أمة وجعلهم أمة وسطا ليكونوا شهداء على الناس؟! ثم كيف امتنعوا عن الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن هذا المنكر الذي هو مخالفة رسول الله عليه السلام وغصب الأمر أهله، والقيام بتنفيذ الأحكام في الدماء والفروج والأموال من غير ثبوت الولاية مع أن الله تعالى وصفهم بالأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر، ومدحهم على ذلك وأثنى به عليهم، أفترى الله تعالى لم يعلم بما يوجد منهم بعد وفاة النبي عليه السلام من تقاعدهم عن الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر، وتسارعهم إلى إعانة المبطل وخذلان المحق حتى وصفهم الله تعالى بذلك وأثنى عليهم به؟! وهذا والله هو الظن المحال والرأي الفاسد والقول الباطل. ثم كيف يظن مسلم أن رهط اختارهم الله تعالى لنصرة رسوله الذي هو خير البشر وصفوة الأنام وخيرته من خلقه، واصطفاهم لصحبته، وأسعدهم بقربه وأكرمهم بدينه الذي نسخ به الأديان وحكم ببقائه إلى الأبد، وأظهر بسيوفهم الدين حتى انتشر في أقاصي البلاد يجمعون على الإعراض عن قبول نصه، وإبطال ما أورثه لأقاربه والانضمام إلى من غصب الحق من صاحبه، ونازع الأمر أهله والاشتغال بنصرته والإطباق على خذلان مستحقه ولم تبرد جلدة نبيه بعد وما مضى من وفاته أسبوع مع أنه سيد المرسلين وإمام المتقين مع بقاء ملة كل من يقدمه من الأنبياء والرسل عليهم السلام الدهر الطويل والزمان المديد؟! ثم أي سبب حمل المهاجرين الأولين والأنصار على ترك النص والإعراض عنه والإقبال على مبايعة غير من نص عليه مع أن من نص عليه باسمه من صميم بني هاشم ولباب بني عبد مناف وخالص ولد قصي بن كلاب وهم الأكثرون عددًا والأوسطون نسبًا والأوفرون محامد ومفاخر ومناقب ومآثر، الأغرون نفسا وديارا، الأمنعون عشيرة وجارًا بل هم المطعمون لأهل المواسم والساقون للحجيج المسمون جيران الله، الوافدون على الملوك المبجلون عند الإقبال المرموقون بعين التبجيل والتعظيم، أصحاب الوفادة والسقاية والسدانة، ومن تقدم عليه وفوض الأمر إليه من بني تميم بن مرة أو عدي بن كعب، ولم يكن لهم من العدة والعديد والبأس الشديد والمال الكثير والأتباع والحواشي نصف ما لأولئك، علم ذلك من عرف التواريخ ووقف على طرف من علم الأنساب وأخبار السلف ولا أنهم عرفوا أنه لا نص لأحد في الخلافة وأن من فوض إليه هو الأحق بذلك من غيره، لاستجماع الفضائل الدينية، والأصلح للقيام بهذا المهم والأقدر على تحصيل ما احتيج إلى نصب الإمام لمراعاته، وبهذه معاني لو تأمل ذو البصيرة ووقف عليها ولم يكابر عقله وأنصف
From the treasury, then the order to return that upon his death to the treasury, and likewise Umar, and likewise the two caliphs after them - may Allah be pleased with them - and if they undertook what was mentioned, then how can it be thought of any one of them that he would turn away from accepting the established text (nass) from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and adhere to its violation?! And if one of them had strayed from his guidance and deviated from the right path and preferred opposition to the Messenger, peace be upon him, and did not care about the wrath of Allah Almighty out of desire to accumulate worthless things and seek abundant unlawful gain because of the severity of soul and evil disposition with which he was created, how would the noble Companions and the leading Emigrants and Helpers and the scholars of the community and the best of the caliphs, whom Allah Almighty testified to be the best community and made them a middle community to be witnesses over people, have assisted him in that?! Then how would they have refrained from enjoining good and forbidding this evil, which is opposition to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and usurpation of the office from its rightful people, and carrying out judgments concerning blood, private parts, and wealth without valid authority, while Allah Almighty described them as enjoining good and forbidding evil, and praised them for that and commended them for it? Do you think Allah Almighty did not know what would occur from them after the death of the Prophet, peace be upon him, of their failure to enjoin good and forbid evil, and their hastening to assist the false and abandon the true, until Allah Almighty described them with that and praised them for it? This, by Allah, is impossible conjecture, corrupt opinion, and false speech. Then how can a Muslim think that a group chosen by Allah Almighty to support His Messenger, who is the best of mankind, the elite of creation, and His chosen from His creatures, and whom He selected for His companionship, and made them happy by his nearness and honored them with His religion (with) which He abrogated the religions and decreed its permanence forever, and through their swords He manifested the religion until it spread in the farthest regions, that they would agree to turn away from accepting his text (nass), to nullify what he bequeathed to his relatives, to join the one who usurped the right from its owner, to contest the office from its rightful people, to occupy themselves with supporting him, and to conspire to abandon the one entitled to it while the skin of his Prophet had not yet cooled and not a week had passed since his death, even though he is the master of the messengers and the leader of the pious, while the religion of every prophet and messenger who preceded him, peace be upon them, remained for a long time and extended period?! Then what reason could have impelled the first Emigrants and the Helpers to abandon the text (nass) and turn away from it and proceed to pledge allegiance to other than the one designated by it, given that the one designated by it by name is from the very core of Banu Hashim, the essence of Banu Abd Manaf, the pure offspring of Qusayy bin Kilab, and they are the most numerous in number, the most central in lineage, the most abundant in praises, excellences, merits, and noble deeds, the most noble in soul and abode, the most protective of clan and neighbor, indeed they are the feeders of the people at the seasons, the waterers of the pilgrims, the ones called neighbors of Allah, the delegates to kings, honored when entering, looked upon with veneration and esteem, the possessors of the delegation, the watering, and the service, while the one who was given precedence over him and entrusted with the matter was from Banu Tamim bin Murra or Adi bin Ka'b, and they did not have even half of what those had of equipment, numbers, severe might, abundant wealth, followers, and retinue; that is known by whoever knows the histories and is acquainted with a part of the science of genealogies and the reports of the predecessors, and [it is known] that they knew that there is no text (nass) for anyone concerning the caliphate, and that the one to whom the matter was entrusted is more entitled to it than others, due to his possessing religious virtues, being more suitable for carrying out this important task, and more capable of achieving what is needed for the appointment of an imam to take care of; and with these meanings, if a person of insight reflects and pauses upon them, and does not force his intellect and is just...
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage is a sustained rhetorical refutation of the claim that the early caliphs (Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman) ignored an explicit textual designation (nass) from the Prophet Muhammad designating Ali as successor. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, uses a series of rhetorical questions to demonstrate the impossibility of such a scenario.

He begins by referencing the financial integrity of the caliphs (the return of funds to the treasury) to establish their uprightness. Then he poses the key question: if these caliphs were so upright, how could anyone think they would reject an established text (nass) from the Prophet? He then imagines a hypothetical: if one of them had indeed strayed and preferred opposition to the Prophet out of greed, how could the best of the Companions (the Emigrants, Helpers, scholars) have supported him, given that Allah described them as the best community and as those who enjoin good and forbid evil? He further argues that if such a great evil (ignoring the nass and usurping authority) had occurred, the Companions would have been obligated to command good and forbid it; but Allah praised them for enjoining good and forbidding evil, so it is impossible that they failed in this duty. The author labels such a thought as impossible conjecture, corrupt opinion, and false speech.

Next, he extends the argument to the entire group of Companions (the 'rahṭ') chosen by Allah to support His Messenger. He asks how a Muslim could believe that this group, chosen for the best of creation, would collectively agree to reject the Prophet's text (nass), nullify his bequest, support a usurper, and abandon the rightful claimant, all within a week of the Prophet's death—especially given that the designated person (Ali) was from the noblest lineage (Banu Hashim) and held the highest honors (like providing water and service to pilgrims), while the one chosen (Abu Bakr) was from a less prominent tribe (Banu Tamim or Adi) and lacked half their resources.

He concludes that anyone familiar with history, genealogy, and reports of the predecessors knows that there was no nass for anyone regarding the caliphate, and that the one entrusted with it (Abu Bakr) was more entitled due to his religious virtues and suitability for the role. The passage ends with an invitation for reflection and fairness, implying that the evidence leads to this conclusion.

Key Terms
نص
خلافة
الصحابة
الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the early caliphs consciously rejected a nass from the Prophet designating Ali.
Correction: Nasafi argues that their known integrity and the Companions' obligation to enjoin good make this impossible.

Checkpoint
What premise does Nasafi use to establish the caliphs' trustworthiness?
A) Their military victories
B) Their handling of public funds
C) Their extensive knowledge
D) Their lineage

Key Takeaway
Nasafi's argument shows that the early caliphs' known integrity makes it rationally impossible for them to have ignored a textual designation from the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the early caliphs' integrity made it impossible for them to reject a clear command from Allah, what does your own integrity say about your willingness to obey Allah's commands when they inconvenience you? Will you examine one area where you have been compromising and commit to change?
?
The Companions are praised for actively enjoining good and forbidding evil. When was the last time you spoke out against an injustice or sin you witnessed? What held you back—fear, apathy, or self-interest? How can you prepare yourself to act like the Companions starting today?
?
Nasafi argues that it is 'impossible conjecture' to think the Companions would remain silent about a great evil. Is there a truth about Islam or a moral issue that you remain silent about in your community? Are you willing to break that silence, even if it costs you comfort or reputation? What is one concrete step you can take this week?

The Chosen Group Could Not Agree to Reject a Nass
Nasafi argues the collective infallibility of the Companions prevents rejection of nass

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that the entire group of Companions, chosen by Allah, could not have conspired to ignore a textual designation.

Core Idea
The best community cannot collectively abandon a clear divine command.

Nasafi extends his argument to the entire group of Companions—the best community. He asks how a Muslim could think that these chosen individuals would agree to reject the Prophet's nass and support a usurper. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the rhetorical structure and the strong language.
Nasafi uses a single long question to make his point.
2
Identify the group described
The passage describes the Companions as chosen by Allah, the best community, selected to support His Messenger. Note the attributes listed.
3
Understand the impossible scenario
Nasafi asks how this group could agree to reject the nass, nullify the Prophet's bequest, and support a usurper. The time factor (within a week of the Prophet's death) adds to the impossibility.
This argument relies on the collective infallibility of the Companions as a group.

من بيت المال، ثم الأمر برد ذلك عند وفاته إلى بيت المال، وكذا عمره، وكذا الخليفتان بعدهما - رضي الله عنهما - وإذا كان تقلدهم لما ذكر فكيف يظن بواحد منهم الإعراض عن قبول النص الثابت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والتمسك بمخالفته؟! ولو أن واحدا منهم ضل عن رشده وزاغ عن الهدى وآثر مخالفة الرسول عليه السلام، ولم يبال من مقت الله تعالى رغبة منه في استجماع الحطام والاسكثار من الحرام لما جبل عليه من شدة النفس وشؤم الطبع، كيف ساعده على ذلك نجباء الصحابة وكبار المهاجرين والأنصار وعلماء الأمة، وخيار الخليفة الذين شهد الله تعالى لهم بكونهم خير أمة وجعلهم أمة وسطا ليكونوا شهداء على الناس؟! ثم كيف امتنعوا عن الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن هذا المنكر الذي هو مخالفة رسول الله عليه السلام وغصب الأمر أهله، والقيام بتنفيذ الأحكام في الدماء والفروج والأموال من غير ثبوت الولاية مع أن الله تعالى وصفهم بالأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر، ومدحهم على ذلك وأثنى به عليهم، أفترى الله تعالى لم يعلم بما يوجد منهم بعد وفاة النبي عليه السلام من تقاعدهم عن الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر، وتسارعهم إلى إعانة المبطل وخذلان المحق حتى وصفهم الله تعالى بذلك وأثنى عليهم به؟! وهذا والله هو الظن المحال والرأي الفاسد والقول الباطل. ثم كيف يظن مسلم أن رهط اختارهم الله تعالى لنصرة رسوله الذي هو خير البشر وصفوة الأنام وخيرته من خلقه، واصطفاهم لصحبته، وأسعدهم بقربه وأكرمهم بدينه الذي نسخ به الأديان وحكم ببقائه إلى الأبد، وأظهر بسيوفهم الدين حتى انتشر في أقاصي البلاد يجمعون على الإعراض عن قبول نصه، وإبطال ما أورثه لأقاربه والانضمام إلى من غصب الحق من صاحبه، ونازع الأمر أهله والاشتغال بنصرته والإطباق على خذلان مستحقه ولم تبرد جلدة نبيه بعد وما مضى من وفاته أسبوع مع أنه سيد المرسلين وإمام المتقين مع بقاء ملة كل من يقدمه من الأنبياء والرسل عليهم السلام الدهر الطويل والزمان المديد؟! ثم أي سبب حمل المهاجرين الأولين والأنصار على ترك النص والإعراض عنه والإقبال على مبايعة غير من نص عليه مع أن من نص عليه باسمه من صميم بني هاشم ولباب بني عبد مناف وخالص ولد قصي بن كلاب وهم الأكثرون عددًا والأوسطون نسبًا والأوفرون محامد ومفاخر ومناقب ومآثر، الأغرون نفسا وديارا، الأمنعون عشيرة وجارًا بل هم المطعمون لأهل المواسم والساقون للحجيج المسمون جيران الله، الوافدون على الملوك المبجلون عند الإقبال المرموقون بعين التبجيل والتعظيم، أصحاب الوفادة والسقاية والسدانة، ومن تقدم عليه وفوض الأمر إليه من بني تميم بن مرة أو عدي بن كعب، ولم يكن لهم من العدة والعديد والبأس الشديد والمال الكثير والأتباع والحواشي نصف ما لأولئك، علم ذلك من عرف التواريخ ووقف على طرف من علم الأنساب وأخبار السلف ولا أنهم عرفوا أنه لا نص لأحد في الخلافة وأن من فوض إليه هو الأحق بذلك من غيره، لاستجماع الفضائل الدينية، والأصلح للقيام بهذا المهم والأقدر على تحصيل ما احتيج إلى نصب الإمام لمراعاته، وبهذه معاني لو تأمل ذو البصيرة ووقف عليها ولم يكابر عقله وأنصف
From the treasury, then the order to return that upon his death to the treasury, and likewise Umar, and likewise the two caliphs after them - may Allah be pleased with them - and if they undertook what was mentioned, then how can it be thought of any one of them that he would turn away from accepting the established text (nass) from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and adhere to its violation?! And if one of them had strayed from his guidance and deviated from the right path and preferred opposition to the Messenger, peace be upon him, and did not care about the wrath of Allah Almighty out of desire to accumulate worthless things and seek abundant unlawful gain because of the severity of soul and evil disposition with which he was created, how would the noble Companions and the leading Emigrants and Helpers and the scholars of the community and the best of the caliphs, whom Allah Almighty testified to be the best community and made them a middle community to be witnesses over people, have assisted him in that?! Then how would they have refrained from enjoining good and forbidding this evil, which is opposition to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and usurpation of the office from its rightful people, and carrying out judgments concerning blood, private parts, and wealth without valid authority, while Allah Almighty described them as enjoining good and forbidding evil, and praised them for that and commended them for it? Do you think Allah Almighty did not know what would occur from them after the death of the Prophet, peace be upon him, of their failure to enjoin good and forbid evil, and their hastening to assist the false and abandon the true, until Allah Almighty described them with that and praised them for it? This, by Allah, is impossible conjecture, corrupt opinion, and false speech. Then how can a Muslim think that a group chosen by Allah Almighty to support His Messenger, who is the best of mankind, the elite of creation, and His chosen from His creatures, and whom He selected for His companionship, and made them happy by his nearness and honored them with His religion (with) which He abrogated the religions and decreed its permanence forever, and through their swords He manifested the religion until it spread in the farthest regions, that they would agree to turn away from accepting his text (nass), to nullify what he bequeathed to his relatives, to join the one who usurped the right from its owner, to contest the office from its rightful people, to occupy themselves with supporting him, and to conspire to abandon the one entitled to it while the skin of his Prophet had not yet cooled and not a week had passed since his death, even though he is the master of the messengers and the leader of the pious, while the religion of every prophet and messenger who preceded him, peace be upon them, remained for a long time and extended period?! Then what reason could have impelled the first Emigrants and the Helpers to abandon the text (nass) and turn away from it and proceed to pledge allegiance to other than the one designated by it, given that the one designated by it by name is from the very core of Banu Hashim, the essence of Banu Abd Manaf, the pure offspring of Qusayy bin Kilab, and they are the most numerous in number, the most central in lineage, the most abundant in praises, excellences, merits, and noble deeds, the most noble in soul and abode, the most protective of clan and neighbor, indeed they are the feeders of the people at the seasons, the waterers of the pilgrims, the ones called neighbors of Allah, the delegates to kings, honored when entering, looked upon with veneration and esteem, the possessors of the delegation, the watering, and the service, while the one who was given precedence over him and entrusted with the matter was from Banu Tamim bin Murra or Adi bin Ka'b, and they did not have even half of what those had of equipment, numbers, severe might, abundant wealth, followers, and retinue; that is known by whoever knows the histories and is acquainted with a part of the science of genealogies and the reports of the predecessors, and [it is known] that they knew that there is no text (nass) for anyone concerning the caliphate, and that the one to whom the matter was entrusted is more entitled to it than others, due to his possessing religious virtues, being more suitable for carrying out this important task, and more capable of achieving what is needed for the appointment of an imam to take care of; and with these meanings, if a person of insight reflects and pauses upon them, and does not force his intellect and is just...
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage is a sustained rhetorical refutation of the claim that the early caliphs (Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman) ignored an explicit textual designation (nass) from the Prophet Muhammad designating Ali as successor. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, uses a series of rhetorical questions to demonstrate the impossibility of such a scenario.

He begins by referencing the financial integrity of the caliphs (the return of funds to the treasury) to establish their uprightness. Then he poses the key question: if these caliphs were so upright, how could anyone think they would reject an established text (nass) from the Prophet? He then imagines a hypothetical: if one of them had indeed strayed and preferred opposition to the Prophet out of greed, how could the best of the Companions (the Emigrants, Helpers, scholars) have supported him, given that Allah described them as the best community and as those who enjoin good and forbid evil? He further argues that if such a great evil (ignoring the nass and usurping authority) had occurred, the Companions would have been obligated to command good and forbid it; but Allah praised them for enjoining good and forbidding evil, so it is impossible that they failed in this duty. The author labels such a thought as impossible conjecture, corrupt opinion, and false speech.

Next, he extends the argument to the entire group of Companions (the 'rahṭ') chosen by Allah to support His Messenger. He asks how a Muslim could believe that this group, chosen for the best of creation, would collectively agree to reject the Prophet's text (nass), nullify his bequest, support a usurper, and abandon the rightful claimant, all within a week of the Prophet's death—especially given that the designated person (Ali) was from the noblest lineage (Banu Hashim) and held the highest honors (like providing water and service to pilgrims), while the one chosen (Abu Bakr) was from a less prominent tribe (Banu Tamim or Adi) and lacked half their resources.

He concludes that anyone familiar with history, genealogy, and reports of the predecessors knows that there was no nass for anyone regarding the caliphate, and that the one entrusted with it (Abu Bakr) was more entitled due to his religious virtues and suitability for the role. The passage ends with an invitation for reflection and fairness, implying that the evidence leads to this conclusion.

Key Terms
رهط
المهاجرون
الأنصار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Companions were fallible individuals who could have made a mistake about the succession.
Correction: Nasafi argues that as a group chosen by Allah, their collective decision cannot be wrong.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, within what time frame did the alleged conspiracy to ignore the nass occur?
A) A day
B) A week
C) A month
D) A year

Key Takeaway
Nasafi argues that the Companions, as the best community chosen by Allah, could not have collectively rejected a nass from the Prophet, especially so soon after his death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that the Companions could not have rejected a clear nass from the Prophet, how does that shape your trust in the historical reports about the early caliphate? Are you willing to accept that your own understanding of those events might be incomplete if it contradicts this principle?
?
Nasafi emphasizes the timing—within a week of the Prophet's death. When you consider your own response to a loved one's last wishes, do you uphold them immediately or allow time to erode your commitment? What does your answer reveal about the strength of your faith?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
6 min
The Case Against a Nass: Nobility and Entitlement
Nasafi uses lineage and history to prove no nass existed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that if there were a nass, it would have been for Banu Hashim, and that history shows there was no nass, so Abu Bakr's caliphate is justified.

Core Idea
Lineage and virtue point to the rightful successor, but no nass existed.

Nasafi turns to the argument from lineage: the one allegedly designated by nass was from the noblest family, while the one chosen (Abu Bakr) was from a less prominent tribe. He concludes that anyone familiar with history knows there was no nass. This lesson examines that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Pay attention to the comparison between Banu Hashim and the tribe of Abu Bakr. Note the detailed descriptions.
2
Understand the question posed
Nasafi asks why the Emigrants and Helpers would abandon the nass if the designated person was from the noble Banu Hashim.
3
Analyze the comparison
Nasafi contrasts the high status of Banu Hashim with the lesser status of Banu Tamim or Adi. The implication is that if there were a nass, it would be for the more noble family.
4
Note the historical conclusion
Nasafi asserts that anyone who knows history knows there was no nass, and that Abu Bakr was more entitled due to his virtues.
This is the key conclusion of the entire refutation.

Commentary
This passage is a sustained rhetorical refutation of the claim that the early caliphs (Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman) ignored an explicit textual designation (nass) from the Prophet Muhammad designating Ali as successor. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, uses a series of rhetorical questions to demonstrate the impossibility of such a scenario.

He begins by referencing the financial integrity of the caliphs (the return of funds to the treasury) to establish their uprightness. Then he poses the key question: if these caliphs were so upright, how could anyone think they would reject an established text (nass) from the Prophet? He then imagines a hypothetical: if one of them had indeed strayed and preferred opposition to the Prophet out of greed, how could the best of the Companions (the Emigrants, Helpers, scholars) have supported him, given that Allah described them as the best community and as those who enjoin good and forbid evil? He further argues that if such a great evil (ignoring the nass and usurping authority) had occurred, the Companions would have been obligated to command good and forbid it; but Allah praised them for enjoining good and forbidding evil, so it is impossible that they failed in this duty. The author labels such a thought as impossible conjecture, corrupt opinion, and false speech.

Next, he extends the argument to the entire group of Companions (the 'rahṭ') chosen by Allah to support His Messenger. He asks how a Muslim could believe that this group, chosen for the best of creation, would collectively agree to reject the Prophet's text (nass), nullify his bequest, support a usurper, and abandon the rightful claimant, all within a week of the Prophet's death—especially given that the designated person (Ali) was from the noblest lineage (Banu Hashim) and held the highest honors (like providing water and service to pilgrims), while the one chosen (Abu Bakr) was from a less prominent tribe (Banu Tamim or Adi) and lacked half their resources.

He concludes that anyone familiar with history, genealogy, and reports of the predecessors knows that there was no nass for anyone regarding the caliphate, and that the one entrusted with it (Abu Bakr) was more entitled due to his religious virtues and suitability for the role. The passage ends with an invitation for reflection and fairness, implying that the evidence leads to this conclusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Abu Bakr was chosen despite a nass for Ali because of tribal politics.
Correction: Nasafi argues that if there were a nass, the more noble Banu Hashim would have been chosen; history shows no nass existed.

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi claim about the existence of a nass for anyone in the caliphate?
A) There was a nass for Ali but it was ignored
B) There was a nass for Abu Bakr
C) There was no nass for anyone
D) There was a nass for both

Key Takeaway
Nasafi concludes that historical and genealogical knowledge shows no nass existed, and that Abu Bakr's selection was based on merit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter historical evidence that challenges a deeply held belief of your community or family, do you have the courage to honestly re-examine your position, or do you 'force your intellect' to cling to what is comfortable?
?
Nasafi argues that the early Muslims knew there was no nass and acted faithfully. Have you ever assumed that because a practice is widespread in your tradition, it must be based on a clear text? What would it cost you to check that assumption?
?
If you were in the position of the Emigrants and Helpers, faced with two candidates—one of noble birth and one of proven piety and ability—which would you choose, and would your choice be based on evidence or sentiment? How does that reflect on your current commitments?

intermediate
6 min
The Implausibility of Ignoring a Nass for the Caliphate
The author rhetorically questions how the Companions could have ignored a nass given the Hashimites' virtues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the early Muhajirun and Ansar could not have ignored a supposed textual designation (nass) for Ali's caliphate, given the superior virtues of Banu Hashim and the historical context.

Core Idea
If a nass existed, the Companions would not have abandoned it for lesser candidates.

This passage presents a powerful rhetorical argument against the Shia claim of a specific textual designation (nass) for Ali's succession. The author highlights the extraordinary virtues of Banu Hashim and contrasts them with the Qurayshi tribes of Abu Bakr and Umar, arguing that if a nass existed, the Companions would not have turned away from it so soon after the Prophet's death. By examining this argument, you will see how historical reasoning is used to defend the Sunni position on the caliphate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal translation. Notice the author's rhetorical style—he begins with a question and then piles up descriptions.
The passage is dense; don't worry about every detail at first.
2
Identify the rhetorical structure
Look for three parts: (1) the rhetorical question about the early Muslims abandoning the nass, (2) the long list of virtues of Banu Hashim, and (3) the contrast with the tribes of Abu Bakr and Umar. How does each part support the conclusion?
The list of virtues is intentionally overwhelming to make the point obvious.
3
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that there is no nass for anyone in the caliphate, and that the one chosen (Abu Bakr) was the most deserving due to his religious virtues. Consider why this conclusion follows from the earlier points.
The final sentence invites the reader to be fair and recognize the misguidance of the Rafidah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأكرمهم بدينه الذي نسخ به الأديان وحكم ببقائه إلى الأبد، وأظهر بسيوفهم الدين حتى انتشر في أقاصي البلاد يجمعون على الإعراض عن قبول نصه، وإبطال ما أورثه لأقاربه والانضمام إلى من غصب الحق من صاحبه، ونازع الأمر أهله والاشتغال بنصرته والإطباق على خذلان مستحقه ولم تبرد جلدة نبيه بعد وما مضى من وفاته أسبوع مع أنه سيد المرسلين وإمام المتقين مع بقاء ملة كل من يقدمه من الأنبياء والرسل عليهم السلام الدهر الطويل والزمان المديد؟! ثم أي سبب حمل المهاجرين الأولين والأنصار على ترك النص والإعراض عنه والإقبال على مبايعة غير من نص عليه مع أن من نص عليه باسمه من صميم بني هاشم ولباب بني عبد مناف وخالص ولد قصي بن كلاب وهم الأكثرون عددًا والأوسطون نسبًا والأوفرون محامد ومفاخر ومناقب ومآثر، الأغرون نفسا وديارا، الأمنعون عشيرة وجارًا بل هم المطعمون لأهل المواسم والساقون للججيج المسمون جيران الله، الوافدون على الملوك المبجلون عند الإقبال المرموقون بعين التبجيل والتعظيم، أصحاب الوفادة والسقاية والسدانة، ومن تقدم عليه وفوض الأمر إليه من بني تميم بن مرة أو عدي بن كعب، ولم يكن لهم من العدة والعديد والبأس الشديد والمال الكثير والأتباع والحواشي نصف ما لأولئك، علم ذلك من عرف التواريخ ووقف على طرف من علم الأنساب وأخبار السلف ولا أنهم عرفوا أنه لا نص لأحد في الخلافة وأن من فوض إليه هو الأحق بذلك من غيره، لاستجماع الفضائل الدينية، والأصلح للقيام بهذا المهم والأقدر على تحصيل ما احتيج إلى نصب الإمام لمراعاته، وبهذه معاني لو تأمل ذو البصيرة ووقف عليها ولم يكابر عقله وأنصف الإمامة وعرف ضلال الروافض وافتراءهم على أصحاب رسول الله عليه السلام.
And He honored them with His religion which abrogated the religions and decreed its perpetuity forever, and He manifested the religion by their swords until it spread to the farthest lands. They agreed to turn away from accepting His text (nass), and to nullify what He had bequeathed to His relatives, and to join the one who usurped the right from its owner, and disputed the affair with its people, and to occupy themselves with supporting him, and to agree upon abandoning its rightful owner, while the skin of their Prophet had not yet cooled, and not a week had passed since his death, even though he is the master of the messengers and the leader of the pious, while the religion of every prophet and messenger who preceded him remained for a long time and extended period?! Then what reason caused the first Muhajirun and Ansar to abandon the nass and turn away from it, and to proceed to pledge allegiance to other than the one designated (nass 'alayhi), even though the one designated by name is from the core of Banu Hashim, the pith of Banu Abd Manaf, the pure offspring of Qusayy ibn Kilab, and they are the most numerous in number, the most central in lineage, the most abundant in praises, excellences, merits, and noble deeds, the most noble in soul and abode, the most protective of clan and neighbor. Nay, they are the feeders of the people of the seasons, the waterers of the pilgrims, those called the neighbors of God, the delegates to kings, honored upon arrival, looked upon with the eye of veneration and glorification, the possessors of deputation, watering, and service. And those who were given precedence over him and to whom the affair was entrusted from Banu Tamim ibn Murra or Adi ibn Ka'b did not have half of what those had in terms of numbers, multitude, severe might, abundant wealth, followers and retinue. That is known by whoever knows history and is acquainted with a portion of genealogy and reports of the predecessors. And [it is known] that they recognized that there is no nass for anyone in the caliphate, and that the one to whom the affair was entrusted is the most deserving of it than others, due to his accumulation of religious virtues, and his being most suitable for undertaking this important matter, and most capable of achieving what is needed for appointing an imam to take care of. And with these meanings, if a possessor of insight were to ponder and stop [to consider] them, and not argue against his intellect, and be fair about the imamate, and recognize the misguidance of the Rafidah and their slander against the Companions of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage is a rhetorical refutation of the Shia claim that there was an explicit textual designation (nass) for Ali's caliphate. The author begins by marveling at the suggestion that the early Muslims—the Muhajirun and Ansar—would have abandoned such a nass and pledged allegiance to someone else, given that the designated person (purportedly Ali) was from Banu Hashim, who are described with superlative virtues: they are the most numerous, noblest in lineage, most generous, most protective, feeders of pilgrims, waterers of the hajjis, called neighbors of God, honored by kings, and possessors of the offices of deputation, watering, and service to the Kaaba. In contrast, those who were given precedence (Abu Bakr and Umar, from Banu Tamim and Banu Adi) did not have even half the numbers, might, wealth, and followers of the Hashimites. The author then states that anyone familiar with history and genealogy knows that there is no nass for anyone in the caliphate, and that the one chosen (Abu Bakr) was the most deserving due to his religious virtues and suitability. The conclusion is that if a fair-minded person reflects on these points without stubbornness, he will be fair about the imamate and recognize the falsehood of the Rafidah's claims against the Companions.

Key Terms
النص (nass)
الإمامة (imamate)
المهاجرون (Muhajirun)
الأنصار (Ansar)
بني هاشم (Banu Hashim)
الروافض (Rafidah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the early Muslims ignored a nass due to ignorance or worldly motives.
Correction: The author argues that their actions prove no nass existed, because given the Hashimites' virtues, they would not have turned away from it.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what makes it inconceivable that the Muhajirun and Ansar would ignore a textual designation (nass) for the caliphate?
A) The designated person was from Banu Hashim, who were superior in numbers, lineage, and virtues.
B) The Muhajirun and Ansar were all hypocrites.
C) The nass was not written down.
D) The Prophet forbade writing anything after his death.

Key Takeaway
The early Muslims' unanimous pledge to Abu Bakr, despite the Hashimites' superior virtues, confirms that there was no explicit textual designation for Ali's caliphate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear claims that the early Muslims conspired against Ali, does your heart feel any doubt? Are you willing to trust the unanimous consensus of the Companions even when it challenges your own preferences or group loyalties? What would it take for you to submit to the evidence as presented in this passage?
?
The author argues that the Companions' actions prove the absence of a nass. If you were in their position, would you have had the courage to set aside tribal and familial connections for what you believed to be right? What does that say about your own attachment to family honor or group identity?
?
Do you find yourself defending certain beliefs based on feelings or inherited loyalties rather than on evidence from the sources? This lesson invites you to examine your intellect fairly. Are you willing to let go of any mistaken notion you may have held about the early Muslims' motives, even if it means revising a deeply held view?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
6 min
Ali's Courage Proves No Nass
The author argues Ali's courage proves he would have fought for his right if he had a nass.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses Ali's character and his own recorded statements to argue that no textual designation (nass) existed for him.

Core Idea
Ali's courage proves he would never have remained silent if he had a divine mandate.

In this passage, the author presents a character-based argument against the Shia claim that Ali had a nass. He argues that if such a designation existed, Ali's well-known fearlessness and his own recorded statements would have compelled him to fight for his right. Instead, Ali's peaceful acceptance of Abu Bakr's caliphate shows no nass existed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the flow: description of Ali's character, then two quotes from his letter, then the conclusion.
The passage uses a logical conditional: 'if nass existed, then Ali would have fought.'
2
Identify the key elements
Identify the description of Ali's bravery (e.g., 'la takhudhuhu fi Allah lawmatu la'im'), and the two quotes from his letter to Uthman ibn Hunayf.
The quotes are vivid and show Ali's determination to fight even against overwhelming odds.
3
Understand the logical argument
The author argues: (1) Ali was extremely brave and would not leave truth for weakness. (2) If he had a nass, he would have fought for it. (3) He did not fight. (4) Therefore, no nass existed.
This is an argument from silence combined with character evidence.
4
Consider the counterargument
Some might say Ali's silence was due to political expediency or fear. The author preempts this by emphasizing his fearlessness and using his own words to show he would act.
The common misunderstanding is that Ali was afraid; the author proves otherwise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لو كان نص على علي لما تركه على أن عليا الله كان ممن لا تأخذه في الله لومة لائم، ولا يترك الحق لضعف أو هوادة، وهو الموصوف بالصلابة في الدين الموسوم بالشجاعة والبسالة ورباطة الجأش وشدة الشكيمة وقوة الصرعة المشهور له بالبأس والنجدة والظفر في معادن المصاولة وأماكن المبارزة، والمقاتلة على المشهورين من الفرسان والمعروفين من الشجعان بل هو القائل في كتابه إلى عامله عثمان بن حنيف: والله لو ارتدت العرب عن حنيفية أحمد لخضت إليها المنايا، ولضربتهم ضربًا يفض الهام ويرض العظام حتى يحكم الله بيني وبينهم وهو خير الحاكمين، وكذا هو القائل في هذا الكتاب أيضا من لم يبال مني حتفه عليه ساقط، فجنانه في الملمات رابط، فلو كان عرف من النبي عليه السلام فيه أو في عمه العباس نصا وعرف أن لا حق لغيرهما فيه لما انقاد لغيره بل اخترط سيفه وخاض المعركة وطلب حقه أو حق عمه، ولم يرض بالذل والهوان، ولم ينقد لأحد على غير الحق، ولم يتابعه في أموره ولم يخاطبه بخلافة الرسول عليه السلام، ولم يساعد أيضا من الأمر بعده بتقليده ولا زوجه بنته وهو ظالم عليه بغصبه حقه وعاص الله تولى
If there were a nass on Ali, he would not have left it. Indeed, Ali (may God be pleased with him) was among those whom the blame of a blamer does not overtake in the matter of God, and he does not leave the truth due to weakness or lenience. He is described as firm in religion, marked by courage, valor, composure, severity of resolve, strength of fall, famous for valor, succor, and triumph in the arenas of combat and places of dueling, and for fighting against the most famous of horsemen and known champions. Rather, he is the one who said in his letter to his governor Uthman ibn Hunayf: 'By God, if the Arabs apostatize from the Hanifiyya of Ahmad, I would plunge into death to meet them, and I would strike them a blow that splits the skull and crushes the bones until God judges between me and them, and He is the best of judges.' And likewise he said in this book: 'Whoever does not care about his death upon my enmity falls; his mind remains steadfast in calamities.' So if he had known from the Prophet (peace be upon him) a nass concerning himself or his uncle al-Abbas, and knew that no one else had a right in it, he would not have submitted to anyone else; rather he would have drawn his sword, plunged into battle, demanded his right or the right of his uncle, and would not be content with humiliation and disgrace, and would not submit to anyone unjustly, and would not follow him in his affairs, and would not address him as 'Successor of the Messenger of God', nor would he have assisted anyone after him by appointing him, nor would he have married his daughter to him while he was an oppressor against him by usurping his right and disobeying God. Then [someone] took charge.
Source pages p. 468

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and character-based argument (istidlal bi-sifat al-shakhs) against the Shia claim that Ali had a textual designation (nass). The author argues that if such a nass existed, Ali would not have remained silent or submitted to the rule of Abu Bakr and Umar, given his known character. The passage first describes Ali's fearlessness: he is not deterred by blame in God's cause, does not abandon truth for weakness or lenience, and is renowned for firmness, courage, composure, and strength in battle. The author then quotes from Ali's own letter to his governor Uthman ibn Hunayf (found in Nahj al-Balagha), where Ali says he would fight the Arabs if they apostatized. Additionally, another saying of Ali is cited: the one who disregards death is steadfast in calamities. From these, the author concludes that if Ali had known of a nass for himself or his uncle al-Abbas, he would not have accepted the caliphate of others. He would have drawn his sword, demanded his right, refused to address Abu Bakr as 'khalifat Rasul Allah', would not have aided in the appointment of others, and would not have married his daughter to Umar (who is portrayed as usurping his right). Since none of these actions occurred, it proves no nass existed.

Key Terms
النص (nass)
علي (Ali)
الشجاعة (courage)
المقاتلة (fighting)
الصحابة (Companions)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ali's silence was due to fear or political expediency.
Correction: The author cites Ali's well-known courage and his own statements to show he would not remain silent if he had a right.

Checkpoint
On what basis does the author argue that Ali would not have remained silent if he had a textual designation (nass)?
A) Ali's fear of the Quraysh.
B) Ali's well-known courage and his own statements about fighting for truth.
C) A command from the Prophet to fight.
D) The agreement of all Companions.

Key Takeaway
The author proves Ali had no nass by appealing to his courage: if he had one, he would have fought for his right, but he did not.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ali was described as someone who does not leave the truth due to weakness or leniency. In what area of your life are you remaining silent about the truth because you fear the blame of others? Will you commit today to speak or act for the truth, even if you stand alone?
?
The author argues that if Ali had a right, he would have fought for it. You may not have a caliphate to claim, but do you have a right—a truth from Allah—that you are ignoring or not acting upon because it is difficult? What is stopping you from drawing your own 'sword' and standing firm?
?
Ali did not submit to anyone unjustly. Reflect on a time when you submitted to injustice—perhaps through silence, compliance, or fear. How did it feel? Knowing that Ali would not have done so, what will you do differently next time injustice comes before you?
